<Author>PAWahine
<Content>A fun and funky hotel with good location This hotel was recommended to me by the manager of another ResortQuest hotel on the Big Island. My fiance and I got married on the Big Island on Dec 4, 2008. Our families came with us and we all stayed at Waikiki Beach Hotel before the wedding. We were there from Nov. 30-Dec. 3. It was great. The staff was very friendly at the valet and check-in. The hotel was clean and I liked the bright Hawaiian decor. The hotel isn't on the beach, but it is right across the street with nothing in between. A rock wall creates a nice little lagoon for part of the beach which is great for small kids. (My nephew is 8 mos., so it was good for him!) The rest of the beach is awesome Waikiki with a great view of Diamond Head.The hotel is also in a good location. Lots of shops and restaurants and the International Market Place within an easy 20 minute walk. We didn't use public transportation because we had a van, but it looked like there were lots of shuttles, buses and taxis available too. For $9, the hotel has a van that can take you to the airport. I read the other reviews before we left and it seemed that the biggest complaints were about the breakfasts and the elevators. I thought that the breakfasts were good (And they were free and convenient! How can you complain about that?) There was always a hot option with eggs, meat and potatoes. Then, they also had bagels, pastries, cereal, fresh fruit, yogurt, juice and coffee. And the little cooler bags were very cute. I would agree with the elevator complaints though. You have to use your key to access the guest floors and timing is everything. If you don't do it right, you will miss your floor and just ride around. It is supposed to be a form of security, but anyone can get on with you and go to the same floor you do, so I don't know how effective it is. If anything, I think it is just more irritating to guests than intruders. The guest has a specific floor to get to, and intruder that just jumped on behind the guest will go anywhere the elevator takes him.Overall though, I thought it was a good hotel and i would definitely stay there again.

<Author>stuttsNorthCarolina
<Content>Pleasant and relaxing hotel - smokers beware of Hawaii though! My boyfriend and I stayed November 27-Dec. 2 for a long weekend getaway. We were very happy with the location (right across the street from Waikiki beach) and all the things we could walk to. In a short walk you can cover all of Waikiki, catch a free hula dance at Duke Kanahamoku's statue, shop Kalakaua Avenue, relax in Kapiolani Park, and even go off the main streets for a bowl of Japanese noodles or a locals bar. Our only complaint during our whole stay had more to do with Hawaiian state law - specifically that you can NOT smoke inside any building on the islands except private homes, and more frustratingly, in five days of trying we couldn't find a single business where you could have a drink and a smoke at the same time. You have to be 20 feet away from the property line, I guess, so you can't even sit on a patio and smoke while you have your drink. It is SO frustrating when you are on vacation, trying to relax! The best we could find was Duke's Canoe Club in one of the big hotels on Kalakaua, where you can stand on the beach with your drink literally on the property line and as long as you don't get caught too many times, alternately smoke and drink. We felt like naughty teenagers!

<Content>pool area closed too early. 7:30 pm. My wife and I stayed at this hotel Nov. 2, 2008 to Nov. 13, 2008 inclusive. I must say this hotel is clean, in a good location and close to beach. There is no other place to sit and relax with the pool area closed but to go to other hotels who do let patrons sit by the pool and relax even with their pool closed. This to me is a drawback and a real disappointment. Several elderly people who were just sitting and relaxing were even asked to leave the area because the pool is closed. Where else can a person go to relax but to other hotels. While in Waikiki you do not want to be confined to your room but relaxing in the outdoor air. I have addressed this problem with the hotel itself but they do not seem to have any interest in changing their policy. Pity.Tiki's restaurant and bar located near the pool area can become a bit loud during the night with the music from the bar. After a few days you get accustomed to it and tend to live with it. Overall, on a scale of 1 - 10 I would give this hotel a 4.5. I would not stay there again but at nearby hotels that do let their paying customers sit and relax later that 7:30 or 8:00 p.m.

Elevators that only worked half of the time, old, drab decor in the rooms, smelled musty, no vent in bathroom--always damp and foggy, no coffee maker, no ironing board padding, channel changer that was replaced twice until we finally gave up, loud bar music every night, small lousy pool, and that wasn't even the worst of it.  This hotel boasts of a free continental-type breakfast that you can load up into a provided bag and take along with you to the beach or poolside etc.. What is not explained is that the atmosphere is cattle-call like--you must eat between 6:30-8:30. Staff will block off the area at exactly 8:30 so if you are planning on sleeping in--no soup for you!! Provided is small cereals, fruit cups, small muffins, yogurts, coffee  juices, and some sort of disgusting egg burrito or egg and cheese muffin wrapped freshly at 5:00 am and left out for you to grab amongst the 200 other breakfast diners. It was embarrassing, overcrowded. In addition, we called three times over the course of our stay due to our air conditioning not working. They explained that it shuts itself off by sensor--if you are not in the room it doesn't come on--much like those nifty paper towel holders in public bathrooms. On our last night, and out last attempt at sleep, we had to call maintainence at 12:45 a.m. to get the air going again. My husband was furious--if we could have left and stayed elsewhere we would have but our reservation was non-refundable.  Do yourself a big favor--the location of this hotel is its only saving grace. Hopefully we'll laugh about this in the future, but for now I am still shaking my head.

<Author>shell_81_au
<Content>Beautiful Hawaii This hotel is in an A1 location and given that, is very reasonably priced given the rates at other beachfront properties. We stayed in an Ocean View room, and its hard to imagine having a bad day when waking to such a spectaular view of Waikiki Beach. The pro's for this hotel are definitely the location, the generous room size and the friendly and helpful staff who are always willing to assist. The Tiki bar is also a fun place for a late night beverage, giving the hotel a wonderful atmosphere in the evenings. For the purpose of balance, I have to say that the breakfast at the hotel has been reviewed negatively previously. I have to say that the concept itself is great, to be able to take your breakfast onto the beach. However the quality of the breakfast is a bit lacking. The food is not generally hot enough and there is a very limited selection. In addition, the rooms could do with a bit of a rennovation, they are somewhat dated, and the batrooms are cramped and have no vanities. All said, we had an excellent stay at this hotel, and I provide the negatives purely for constructive criticism, as with a little work, this could be a truely amazing hotel. I would happy return regardless.

<Author>StapletonCO
<Content>Awesome hotel on the best part of Waikiki We initially chose to go with the Hilton Hawaiian Village for our 7-day stay (for our 1-year anniversary) in Honolulu but due to major reservation problems on Hilton's behalf (online and on the phone) we decided it was not destined to be (plus if Hilton couldn't even get their reservation system working, what else couldn't they get to work) and so went with our second choice, that being Resortquest Waikiki Beach Hotel. The reservation process went flawlessly (got that Hilton? You missed out on about $3000 in revenue due to your own errors). We chose this hotel based mostly on other tripadvisor reviews and due also to this hotel being located on what we heard was 'the quiet part' of Waikiki (which it is indeed!).Anyhow, the check-in process was a breeze and although I had trouble operating the infamous dreaded elevators, my wife did not. And actually most people there didn't seem to have much trouble operating the elevators.The rooms are nice (meaning they are your standard room), the king bed was stupendously comfy and the lanai view (ocean view) towards the rest of Waikiki (as opposed to Diamondhead) was awesome.We had no qualms at all with the room except that streetnoise outside seemed to escape in through the joints in the sliding glass door out to the lanai. It wasn't a ton of noise coming in and with the A/C on you could hardly hear it but still some people who want library-like quiet might be pissed.At night we slept with earplugs in (habit formed from many vacations ruined by noisy guests in hallways or outside) and I would definitely recommend that just because the streetnoise in the morning (garbage trucks, delivery vans, tour vans, etc) really picks up and without earplugs it definitely can wake you up.The Breakfast on the Beach was the best thing about this hotel. Overall it seemed to be one notch above 'continental' in it's quality but we are not accustomed to eating anything better than cereal for breakfast, therefore having been provided with doughnuts (which go FAST mind you) and french toast sticks and any kind of juice/coffee was absolutely fantastic! Every morning we ate on the beach (beach towels provided there at the breakfast bar by the hotel, nice touch) and watched the beach come to life.I mentioned that this hotel is on the 'quiet' part of Waikiki, which is to say that there are no malls nor shopping centers nor marketplaces nor luau's nor major traffic that is present on the other parts of Waikiki. There are still plenty of people but it overall seemed much less crowded and therefore WAY more relaxing. It seemed that from the Resortquest Circle Hotel westward it got much more crowded and noisy. But from the 2-3 block stretch from the Resortquest Circle Hotel to this hotel, it was much quieter and more peaceful.Lastly here's some notes:-our anniversary dinner was at 'Orchids', a very nice restaurant in the Halekulani Hotel, and we received great service there. -Tiki's Grill and Bar at the Resortquest Waikiki beach hotel had alright food and alright service but nothing to write home about.-ABC Stores are everywhere you look.Overall, we will absolutely come back to Resortquest Waikiki Beach Hotel in the future (maybe for 2nd anniversary next year?) and will absolutely recommend this hotel to family/friends. You'd seriously have to be a fool with insane expectations to find serious flaws in this hotel. We only wish that we had gone to this hotel last year for our honeymoon (we instead went to East Winds Inn at St. Lucia in the Caribbean, where we spent a week surrounded by stuck-up English people and very rude St. Lucians; you can read my review somewhere on TripAdvisor's site).In closing, we very much so miss this hotel's Breakfast on the beach (on the beach) and this hotel's beds.

<Author>traveltosun
<Content>An honest review of an awesome place! I was very disappointed to see the negative reviews for this place. I am very late in writing this review, but I felt I should share the positive experience we had. I was in Honolulu for a convention for 4 days. My family accompanied me, and we had a total of 3 rooms. We picked this place as we like the zoo end better, because of the beach area and it is far less congested. All 6 of us concluded we would recommend this hotel to anyone! Cons: We had an issue with check in. They gave my parents a room key for a room that someone was already in! A bit annoying as this was the only one of our rooms that was ready when we checked in, so we had hauled luggage for 6 people up to the 13th floor to leave it until the other rooms were ready. It was quite a suprise when we opened the door to find there was someone else's luggage in the room! We lugged everything back to the check in desk where we straightened everything out. They gave us a $50 resort credit as compensation for our trouble, which helped make up for the inconvenience and lost hour of our time. The reviews about the room size are true. They are very small, and I would definately not want more than 2 people in them. However, I didn't come to Hawaii to sit in my room. The balcony DOES hold more than 1 person. I know this as 4 members of my family sat outside drinking their wine and watched the Hilton fireworks show! If you're looking to have dinner from your balcony or throw a party, then my suggestion would be to rent a condo or go to a restaurant. There is no air conditioning in the halls or elevators. This wasn't a huge deal, but a little uncomfortable when you have your arms full with shopping bags and/or luggage. We also had an oceanfront room, which was at the very end of the hall.PROS: The staff was very friendly. I came back to my room to gather some things, and the maid was cleaning it. She asked for my room key so she could put it in my door to make sure it was really my room. Some may find this annoying, but I was thrilled she was looking out for my belongings. The beds are WONDERFUL! We met for breakfast the next a.m.  all of us ranted  raved about how good we slept. My mom actually pulled the sheets off her bed to see what kind of mattress it was! While the rooms are small, they are newly renovated and very clean. There are large flat panel tv's in the rooms, and all new furniture including a fridge. Each morning they serve free breakfast by the pool! It isn't a full buffet breakfast, but a couple of steps above a continental breakfast. There is the usual fruit, pastries, muffins, cereal, yogurt, but also a couple of hot items as well and many beverage selections. Each room has portable coolers when you check in. These are awesome, because you can gather fruit, yogurt, etc. to take to your room for later. My family met at the pool every a.m. and enjoyed breakfast together, read the newspapers they provide and listened to the live musician playing soothing hawaiian music. It was a wonderful way to start our day. The location is perfect! Our ages ranged from 30's to 60's. We wamted a place close to everything, but not right in the middle of a bunch of buildings and noisy bars/clubs. This place provided just that. There were several dining options within steps. Tiki's is on site and provides beautiful ocean views, Wolfgang Puk's  Subway are on the street level below, Lulu's is on the 2nd floor of the hotel next door, and there is a Starbucks next door as well! The pool deck is very nice and looks right out at the ocean. I also wanted to note that I was in Honolulu again this past December for a girls getaway. I took my friend to the RQ to show her the pool deck  I noticed the patio furniture was all new and had nice chair pads on all of the loungers. Great addition!! I would highly recommend this hotel. We had a wonderful experience, and we all loved it! I will be back in Honolulu next December running the Honolulu Marathon with a group of friends, and this will be my first choice for our hotel reservation!Tip: There is an ABC store on the street level at the hotel next door (you will actually see hundreds of them!). They have every beverage imaginable and snack foods. You can save some money by buying your own beverages and enjoying them on your balcony versus sitting in the bar and payingt $5 for a beer--it may be even more now!Also, if you're in to trinket  gift shopping go to the Aloha Stadium for the swap meet. It is about 1/2 hour away, but there is a tour company that has roundtrip shuttle service for $6-8 (may be more now?). I can't remember the name of it, but they have a booth in the Park Shore lobby right next door.

<Author>journey99
<Content>Good Choice If Looking For Moderate Budget This hotel is probably one of the best if you are looking for value with a moderate budget in Waikiki. With that you must realize this hotel will not compare to other resorts above 3 stars for Hawaii standards. I stay in Waikiki on business about 6-8 times a year, and have stayed at just about all of the hotels. I decided to try the RQ Waikiki Beach as I prefer the location near the Park and the Zoo as it is less congested and has the best driving access to the freeway H1. The Good: value for price - an Oceanview room for $159 is an excellent value. The location - directly across the street from the best beach on Waikiki and the park. Affordable decent eats (Wolfgang Puck, Subway, Coldstone) are connected to the hotel. The staff are all very friendly and trying to be accomodating. Tiki's has great food although resort prices. Would suggest requesting a balcony table as inside is noisy,The Wish They Could Change: The room sizes are fairly small by hotel standards. I was in a standard oceanview room on the 23rd floor facing Waikiki which was 225 square feet including the balcony in a 2 queen bedded room. For me and another adult - it was a little cramped and I cannot imagine a family of four in the standard room. It would be a little challenging - sort of like a cruise ship room - tiny bathroom, and other than the beds no where to relax in room. The balconies have great views, but they are so tiny only 1 person can be out there at a time, actually there is only 1 chair - and I never observed anyone out relaxing on balcony. The room is clean. The air-conditioning unit does not cool the entire room - it just blows cold air as it is tied to a motion detector.The Bad: The flow of the hotel and those elevators. Ok management, there has been enough feedback here and at the hotel. It's time to fix this. The card-key required elevators have a problem with the card readers in several specific elevators. Some work fine, but most do not. The staff says that the problem is because the guests accidently de-magnitize the keys with cell phones and credit cards. Not true. The keys work fine in the hotel room doors, but not in the elevators. What this boils down to is a rediculous procedure that can be frustrating when you use elevators. I probably only swiped my card 20% of the time I stayed there because you just get on and wait for someone that has a card that works and everyone pushes their numbers. I observed about 60-70% of the time, peoples cards didn't work. Enough on that - it's rediculous - and there is absoulutely no reason (security etc.) for a hotel this size with limited elevators to be card-keyed. Management: get the clue: remove the card readers!Also noteworthy is the wierd flow in this hotel that makes you feel like you are at an airport - queing up to get to place a and b. Most of the elevators stop at the lobby on the second floor - where you have to get out and take another elevator down 1 floor or take the escalator (which most people do). Interesting that this requires that you walk past 3 large tour selling desks each time. Felt like an intentional design to me. Anyways, prepare to feel like you are always schlepping to get in and out of this hotel.Overall - you get what you pay for and in this case I think if you are looking for moderate budget and clean but small accomodations with good location, this is a good choice. Try to ignore the whacky elevators and silly people flow (herding cattle) and you will have a great time!

We were given little insulated bags with which to take to breakfast--served buffet style near the pool. We could then take these to enjoy breakfast at the beach, in our room, or poolside, complete with live Hawaiian music and a hula dancer. It was a wonderful way to begin each day.  There is a great beach right across the street from the hotel. One area is walled in, giving a calmer atmosphere for people that just want to float or play in quieter waters. There is a walkway out into the water with a gazebo which turned out to be a popluar place for the teen locals to jump into the crashing waves. We were quite entertained by this. The beach area had great waves for boarding. The hotel is next door to the zoo, which was a fun thing to do with the kids while my husband was off golfing. It is reasonably priced, too. There are several places to eat right there at the hotel, including Tiki, located in the hotel, Wolfgang Puck Express, Coldstone, Subway, Starbucks, etc.  You can't go wrong with this hotel. We will return!

<Author>tikihoneymoon
<Content>Honeymoon awesomeness My husband and I stayed at RQ Waikiki Beach from 6/2/08 - 6/9/08. We never heard anybody next to us, either, which was nice since we were on our honeymoon! ;-)I will say that if you're looking for good service at Tiki's, you're unlikely to get it. My husband asked the (apparently disgruntled) bartender what he recommended, and he just handed us the drink menu. And then proceeded to ignore us again for a while. We went again a few nights later, and had a similar experience while sitting at a table on the patio. The waitress hardly ever stopped at our table. And the drinks are WAY overpriced. We ended up buying some liquor at the ABC store and keeping it in the fridge in our room. Much more cost-effective.Also, the elevators at RQ are a little odd. You need to swipe your room key in a timely manner, or you will end up bouncing randomly from floor to floor and ending up back where you start. This card-swiping system would be fine, if the mag reader worked more than 30% of the time. It was kind of a joke every time we got on the elevator to see if we could do it right. Not bad, just slightly annoying.Overall, I would highly recommend this hotel to other travellers, and we plan to come back again someday!

<Author>ian1784
<Content>Great location, Great Views Where to start?When we arrived we knew that the room would most likely not be ready for us because we flew in that morning. However, we checked our bags and went upstairs to 'Pre Check-In'. This was great for us as it gave us a chance to tell them that we were Honeymooners, which got us a free upgrade and bottle of sparkling wine in our room (which didn't taste the best). As we had an hour or two to kill we decided to go to the Honolulu Zoo which was just a short walk around the corner. When we returned to the Hotel to collect our room keys the staff were great. We went to our room (room 1702) and as we walked to the door we see this amazing view of Diamond Head (Extinct Volcano), which you can walk up and have an awesome view of all of Waikiki. Then we walked into our room and were pleased as the pictures of the room on the website were just like the room itself. The rooms aren't exactly the biggest, but it was big enough for the two of us. We ended up with an Ocean View Room, which was fantastic.There is alot to do on Oahu including The Polynesian Cultural Center which is a 'not for profit' attraction that shows the differences in Polynesian Cultures. It is run mostly by University students trying to put themseleves through school. Other things to do include - Climbing Diamond Head (which i previously mentioned), The Grand Circle Tour (if you decide to do this, stick to theTour desks recommendations, Pearl Harbour is another big attraction (if you go on a tour, you don't get much time there) We went to Pearl Harbour by Shuttle which cost us $9 each return with a coupon. The line up for the Arizona Memorial is usually very long so get there early to avoid waiting around. You cannot take any type of BAG to the Arizona Memorial, USS Missouri, USS Bowfin or the Aviation Mueseum, They are STRICTLY FORBIDDEN and the will be taken off you if you don't choose to put them in a locker for the day. Also for you Aussies or just people who like to party we went on a pub crawl, we met a guy on the main stretch of Waikiki that looked a bit suss, his name was William, he is African American and the name of the pub crawl is the Endless Summer Pub Crawl we decided to go on the pub crawl, it cost $50 ($30 deposit  $20 on the night) which covered your entry to 5 clubs and a complimentary drink at each... Don't hold your breath for the free dinner it wasn't that great, my recommendation is to eat before you get there... It was good fun.Another thing which My wife and I did was got to a little store called Hilo Hatties, There is a FREE trolley which picks you up outside the ResortQuest Waikiki Beach Hotel every 30 minutes, it also does a couple of courtesy drop offs at the Boat Marina and also the Ala Moana Center which is a good place to shop.Now, back to the Hotel. There are plenty of restaurants downstairs and around the hotel (check the coupon book they give you at check-in and the coupon books on the streets for good deals). The Breakfast on the Beach (BOB) is a good idea, however some days the food didn't appeal to us (menu changes daily). There is plenty of convienience stores (ABC Stores) around, there is a running joke in my family that says that ABC stands for 'All Blocks Covered'.Now to the few bad points that we encountered, Tiki's Bar  Grill have different foods available, but it wasn't the best. But TIki's is a great place to sit around and chill out with a view of the ocean and a few cocktails (We also liked Lulu's Surf Club around the corner). When you walk along the street and people stop you to ask if you have any tours booked they are usually timeshare people, we found the easiest way to get rid of them is to tell them you are leaving early the next morning. There was only one other bad thing which was, Hawaii have passed a law that if you smoke you must be at least 20 feet away from any door, window or vent (which won't affect you non-smokers) but it tends to cause a bit of hassle when you are on the 17th floor and you want a cigarette. Also the bums come up and ask you for cigarettes and they also take the ones that aren't quite finished out of the ashtrays, a solution to this could be to install ashtrays with water in them or something to prevent them walking up and down at late hours of the night.I hope this review has helped you in deciding what hotel and some activities to do on Oahu.

<Author>bigal409
<Content>Just back from Waikiki.... My husband and I just returned from a 7 day stay at Resortquest. The location is great, right across street from beach and next to Honolulu Zoo. Room was on 25th floor with partial ocean view, but out the front door, the view of Diamond Head was amazing. Breakfast on beach was a great addition to price of room. The food wasn't the best, but for FREE, whatca' expect? We stuck with the cereal and fruit bowl each morning. On the hotel block there was Subway, Coldstone, Wolfgang Pucks, ABC store, Starbucks and more. Another helpful thing about the hotel is Expedia is in the lobby and tour-booking place. Although the lady that helped us book some tours (which we ended up cancelling, renting a car and going on our own) was very rude. And the beach is right across the street. If you plan on laying out on the beach, I'd suggest getting there early, and plan ahead for the tide, because it sneaks up on you. Also, if you want to boggie-board, just buy one from ABC store for $20 rather than rent one (we paid $15 for two hours before we found them at ABC). Things to do on the island...We rented a car for two days (highly suggest) and visited North Shore, Dole Plantation, Kahula Beach, Hanumea Bay (closed on Tuesday's), Pali Lookout, Wahamea Falls and much more! Great restaurants within walking distance of hotel were Lulu's (right on corner with hotel), Dukes, Red Lion bar, Cheeseburger in Paradise, Moose McGlightys, Cheesecake Factory, etc. There is a trolley that will take you around town, it's $1 a ride. If you plan on using the trolley more than a couple times, I'd suggest buying a pass for unlimited use. In one of the travelers guide coupon book things, there was a buy one get one free coupon. Also, public bus system is great! Only $2 per person. This bus goes around the entire island if you don't want to rent a car. Overall, our second trip back to Hawaii was great. Although Waikiki is beautiful, it was nice to rent a car and see the rest of the island. I'd highly recommend this hotel b/c of price and location. Our next trip back we'll stay here again!

Our room was a larger one on the 21st floor looking back at Waikiki. It was great. The bathroom had a few small issues, but the lady that cleaned our room did a beautiful job. The one thing I noticed about almost all of the critical reviews was that they had complaints but it did not look like they ever did anything about it. I don't remember big problems, but anytime we needed anything or asked for anything, we were helped immediately. The elevators were very quirky, but we just dealt with it and did not let it bother us. For a older building it was in good shape and always appeared to be taken care of. Three of us spent 10 days and I was very sad to go home. I would recommend that if you need a coffee pot in your room to go buy a cheap one at Walmart. That is what we did. I would stay here again and hope that I get to in the next year or so.

<Author>MissChrisPhoenix_AZ
<Content>All In All, A Nice Place To Stay We stayed at this hotel from May 28th through June 3rd and it was pretty much as we expected it to be. No big surprises, which is how we like it. Having read all the reviews on Tripadvisor, I was aware of some of the issues people had been having so I was prepared to deal with them because this hotel receives some of the best reviews hands down of the same priced hotels on Waikiki Beach.Lets start with Check In. This was as smooth a check-in as you can get. We stayed in an ocean view Junior Suite (room 927) and liked it very much. Sure, it was on the small side and the decor was nothing to write home about but it was clean and free from bed bugs! Housekeping was nice as were all the employees of the hotel that we met. We especially liked the gentleman that worked out at the pool. Very helpful.On to the elevator fiasco. We were prepared for the card-key debacle people had been writing about. About 75 percent of the time, the card key doesn't work on the elevator and then the elevator takes you wherever it wants to go. Some elevators went up when the arrow pointed down and vice-versa. We saw an elevator repair man working three days while we were there but he apparently didn't fix the problem. Knowing about this ahead of time turned what could have been really aggravating to something that became kind of funny. We made a game of it to see which elevator would take us up or down and who's key would work. It's vacation so why let it get to you. I think it would be in the best interest of the hotel to get this resolved soon though.If you want a quiet early night's sleep book your room on the Diamond Head side of the hotel. The band plays until midnight and it is very loud. Thank God for ear plugs! Again, people had written about this in the past so we came prepared. It was worth it for the terrific view we had from our room!Breakfast is another issue that seems to be consistent in all the reviews. Yes its free. It's just okay. For some reason they felt they needed to hide the cream cheese from those of us who wanted a bagel. On our third day I saw a woman ask for some and she was given it from another refrigerator behind where the breakfast bar was. I looked back there the next day and no cream cheese. Why can't they just put it out? After about the 4th day the breakfast was blah. No new choices. By the last day there were no hot choices, no yogurt anymore and of course no cream cheese. And no cereal. At least the coffee was good.Oh yeah, the hotel next door is undergoing renovations and the workers start around 8 am. It can get pretty loud but we were early risers so it didn't bother us too much.I would definitely stay here again even with all the issues. It is in a great place on Waikiki, it's clean and we really didn't have any problems on our entire trip. Just the same annoyances everyone else had but by coming prepared it didn't really bother us too much. We had a great time and I would recommend this hotel to my friends but I would let them know first about the annoyances.

<Author>glansande
<Content>Worked for us! We'll be coming back! I work in hospitality, so I am always very nervous about staying in hotels that aren't mine. At first, I didn't like our standard room on the 5th floor right above the lobby because the view wasn't as good and the room was smallish, and as I was about to fork out more cash for an upgrade, the gentleman at the desk (who also worked SF hospitality at one point) upgraded our room to a double on the 23rd floor with a view of Diamond Head and the ocean. Thank you desk man! This hotel is right on the Waikiki strip, but is on the zoo side on the far end. This was no big deal either, because Waikiki is small and all you'll do is walk. The beds were very comfortable, the service impeccible, and I appreciated the little breakfasts (though we did take advantage of Wolfgang Pucks Express downstairs more than once). The pool has left to be desired, but I wouldn't have used the pool anyway with the beach right there!! This was a vacation with my partner, but I am suggesting this hotel to my family for our Christmas vacation, as it is TOTALLY family friendly too. What a deal!

<Rating>5	5	4	5	5	5	5	5	

<Author>blainehamilton
<Content>Good Place At A Great Value Just finished a stay May 24-30, and I have to say I was impressed. Booked a standard City View room for $129 a night thru the Travelzoo deal posted in their Top 20 deals towards the end of April. For a hotel on Waikiki beach and breakfast included, the price was rediculously cheap. While not perfect, the Hotel is highly suggested.The Good:The location! The hotel is nested right at the South (or East depending how you interpret the direction) end of Waikiki Beach. This keeps the foot and vehicle traffic noise lower during the night hours. It also seemed to keep the undesirables to a minimum. With waikiki beach literally across the street, you can have your toes in the sand after a short 2 minute walk from the lobby. Access to shopping along Waikiki beach is steps away, and attractions such as Honolulu Zoo, Honolulu Aquarium are right next door. Diamond Head is close by, and the H1 freeway is a short distance away, making access to all parts of the island a simple trip.The room! While not as big as some newer hotels, we never had space issues for the two of us. Closet space and drawer space was more than ample for unpacking clothing for a 6 night stay. The furniture was fresh and scratch free, the television a big and bright brand new 32 LG LCD, and the King size bed was incredibly comfy, with fresh linens every day. Ample bath and hand towels, along with shampoo/conditioner/lotions were provided in the bathroom, as well as a hand dryer and backlit makeup mirror. A table and two chairs gave us space to sort out the mountains of magazines, brocures, and coupons one gathers to organize their trip and see everything possible. We were given a 10th floor Pool/Ocean View room without asking, and was wonderful, especially to enjoy breakfast. The balcony was clean and equipped with a chair and stool, and allowed one to sit back and enjoy the waves of the Pacific.The breakfast! The complementary coolers were a great idea, and having an open breakfast from 6:30am to 9:30am allowed both early and late risers to get their fill. Good selection of cereals, danishes, mini muffins, mini bagels, fresh fruit, pudding, coffee (including the kona cononut coffee my wife loves), tea, milk, juices (LOVE the passion guava with a hit of sprite) and soft drinks. This is complemented by a hot item selection that changes every day, which included on differnt days: ham and egg buns, sausage and egg buns, scrambled eggs and bacon, scambled eggs and vegetables, bacon and egg burritos and vegetable and egg burritos. As we were usually up early due to the time difference, I would pick up breakfast just after 6:30am, and we would enjoy in bed, on our balcony overlooking the sea, or on the beach right in front of the hotel accross the street. The musical entertainment with a Hula dancer made sitting by the pool that much more special. Running the breakfast until 9:30am allowed us to pick up a few more fruits and danishes for on the road during the day. Most days we just had light lunches, saving us additional money, thanks to the snacks we could bring along with us.The decor! Some people call it tacky, but then again, wouldn't that make most of hawaii and almost all of it's clothing that way as well? Heck, my entire Hawaiian shirt waredrobe resembles the bedspread. It's the style there, and the hotel pulls it off perfectly. From the Tiki fire torches around the pool/bar/restaurant, to the Green and White surfboards proudly displaying the hotel name in the lower lobby, to the loud red print fabric headboard and bedspead in the room, it just works. We never had the beaded closet doors someone mentioned, but I would welcome them. If I wanted a plain eggshell white room with beige linens, I'll stay at brand x chain hotel. If you want a hotel you can take great photos of and show just as proudly as the other Hawaiian attractions to people, this is the place.The valet/bellmen! When we first arrived, both the valet and bellman were right at my drivers door to take car of us. Speedy service with the bags, and the valet was considerate and even reminded me when I forgot to put our GPS away to prevent theft. While $20 a day isn't cheap for valet, you get top notch service. We would call down 5 to 15 minutes ahead of time before heading to the lower lobby for our vehicle and were never kept waiting longer than a minute or two. In most cases, the car was ready to go when we arrived. I didn't tip every time when picking up or dropping off (you tend not to keep cash in your swim trunks), but made sure they knew I loved the service when I had an extra single on me.The room maintenance! We had a small issue with the tub not draining, and the balcony door sensor for the AC broken when we first arrived. I called the morning we noticed the issues and went down to pick up my car from the valet. I had to return to the room to pick up my forgotten camera, and the maintenance man showed up at that time, less than 15 minutes after making the call. Things were fixed promptly, and he was very professional, and very friendly.The restaurant/bar! Tiki's is one of the most underrated places on the Waikiki beachfront. The food was excellent, the service fast and a real treat. (I wish I could remember the name of our server, since he was a really great guy) The decor is classy and classic at the same time. The view from the patio overlooking the ocean with Tiki torches overhead makes a perfect place for dinner/drinks and the sunset. The music in the bar is great too, sets the mood for chilling with a cold one. Even the Tiki character on the sign and his big statue by the front entrance still gives me a smile when I think about it. Whoever came up with that gets a pat on the back. We only dined once, but the food was delicious, and very reasonable. Dessert was excellent, albeit we had to take it to go and enjoy in our room since we were too full from dinner. The drinks in the bar were mixed well, and beer was ice cold. Best part about both places, is the ability to get a table or place at the bar with next to no wait. Other comparable restaurants/bars like Dukes and The Cheescake Factory usually have a 30 to 60 minute wait for a table, but at Tikis there was space to spare, thanks to being at the quieter end of Waikiki Beach.The Bad:The AC. The Air Conditioner in our room lacked decent airflow, and made more noise than cool air. The first couple of days we were on the island, we were not climatized to the heat and the humidity. On the first 2 nights, we slept with the window open to keep cool with the breeze instead. After that, we found the AC could keep the room at 23 to 24 celcius if we left it on all day and night, otherwise, we came back to a 30 degree sauna in the late afternoon. Any colder was just not possible, no matter how low you set the temp. The old AC unit made a ton of racket too, a steady knocking rattling sound. This kept me from having a decent sleep, so I resorted to sleeping with a pillow over my head. While this sounds extreme, it is rather normal for me, as my wife frequently sleeps with the television on.The cleanliness/finish in the bathroom. While the rest of the room seems spic and span and very recently decorated, the bathroom seems to just have a coat of paint splashed on it and new sink/tub/toilet fixtures. The grout in the floor and splash tiles was dirty, and the walls were a bit scratched and dirty as well. The hair dryer was functional, but had a good chunk of the plastic casing missing, making me question it's safety. One thing that really stuck out was the cleanliness of the lightswitch. It was filthy. Changing these on a regular basis should be considered, since it costs a dollar or two at most and 5 minutes time.Using your cardkey in the elevator. This is a royal pain in the arse, especially if you have your hands full with shopping bags or breakfast. While security of the guests is paramount, nothing stops someone from hopping in the elevator with a guest and punching a random floor when the guest swipes their card instead. I noticed you sometimes had to make several attempts (sometimes 10 or more) to swipe your card before it was accepted. If you don't do it in a timely fashion, the elevator may skip your floor, and you have to do a round trip to the top of the hotel and back down. I would suggest running a wet card reader cleaner in these readers on a regular basis, as the poor read consistency is probably due to dirty mag heads. Even better, just switch it off during the daytime hours of 7am to 7pm and have security check each floor on a regular basis.The apartments/hostels behind the hotel. The dumpy 4 story apartment/hostel buildings behind the hotel creates a lousy atmosphere for guests whose rooms overlook this area. The guests of those buildings regularly gather in front late at night and make a fair bit of noise, and leave garbage in front of their buildings. We noted the police breaking up 'gatherings' on more than a couple of occasions late at night during our 6 night stay. I did take a stroll by these buildings take one night, and was greeted by a couple of aloha's and one friendly greeting of 'do you want to get high?'. As long as you steer clear of the backside area of the hotel at night, you should be fine.As you can see, the good things about this hotel FAR outweigh the bad. The renovations and new look of the hotel are obvious pluses. If you can still get the $129 deal thru Travelzoo, which includes dates in Sept and beyond IIRC, go for it. Many thanks to the staff at Resortquest Waikiki Beach, you made our trip very memorable.

<Author>jvmaddux
<Content>medium priced hotel, medium priced quality We stayed in room 734....ocean front room...from May 20 through May 28th.The view was amazing! It was great sitting on the balcony looking at the ocean, and watching all of the people.The hotel is advertised as recently remodelled. And, it does have fresh paint, newer decorations, new carpeting and a flat screen t.v. However, it is still a very old hotel. And, the renovations were not of the highest quality.The bathroom door had probably 20 layers of paint applied over the years, and the paint was chipping off. The Bathroom floor tile had black mildew looking stains, and cracked tile. The bathtub surrond appeared to be new. However, it was just a cheap plastic insert. This is basically a Motel 6 with a flat screen t.v. and great view.The breakfast on the beach was free...so, I hate to be negative...but, it tasted free....pre-processed, institutional type food. The eggs did not appear to be real eggs, but, some kind of egg substitute, they served them in a plastic container with four soggy tater-tots. The breakfast burrito, had these same fake eggs rolled into a tortilla. The fresh fruit was good, the coffee was good, and of course, they had boxed cereal and danishes. However, this is not a scrumptious breakfast as many reviews would lead you to believe. We gave the hotel breakfast four trys...and then could simply not stomach it any more, and chose McDonalds over this stuff!!!The staff was mostly friendly, and the rooms were mostly clean. There was some dust on the overhang curtain that was above the bed. Upon check-in, the bell man was rather insistent on taking our luggage, and we were on vacation, so thought...sure, why not....he said it would be in our room when we checked in. Check in only took five minutes...and when we arrived in our room, there were no bags...we waited nearly 45 minutes for our bags to arrive!....that was a drag...excited about being in Hawaii...and just wanted to jump in the ocean...but, had to wait for our bags for our swimsuits....so, do not let the bell men take your luggage.The Tiki's bar and grill is located just several floors beneath our room. And, while it was fun watching people, enjoying the music, etc... The rooms are not insulated well....and the inebriated chatter became louder as the night progressed and continued until closing at 1 a.m. each morning. In addition, they have a live band that plays until 12 p.m. I didn't expect the bar noise would bother me...as I assumed I would be up later than I was...However, because of jet-lag, and time difference....I was in bed several nights by 10 p.m.....and it was nearly impossible to sleep...I bought some ear plugs that helped some....but the bar and grill is noisy.The hotel really needs to invest in some sound proof insulation, and multi-layed glass patio doors to block this noise when not wanted.With all of this said...this was a medium priced hotel overlooking the ocean...so, I did not expect a Lodge of the 4 Seasons, or W. The hotel was adequate, and probably a good one for the price.Would I stay here again if the price were right? Not unless, I was assured that the rooms were insulated from the noise...when I want to sleep...I want to sleep. Should you stay here? If you are sure you can stay up past midnight....regardless of jet lag....and, if staying at a Motel 6 type hotel does not bother you...sure, this is a good bargain. But, if you are looking for a plush hotel, and plenty of early sleep...this place is not for you.I am amazed at all of the other reviews on this site....it makes me think they must be planted by the hotel....most everyone I spoke with at the hotel had the same general impression...not very impressed...and were upset by the noise from the bar and grill....interesting not many mention these kinda important facts.

<Content>Too many good things to say!! My family and I traveled to Oahu for the first time a few weeks ago, and while trying to plan our trip we found choosing where to stay to be a very daunting task. We found a deal for the Resortquest Waikiki Beach Hotel from Travelzoo.com. After reading reviews from others on tripadvisor.com, we decided to book. I must say my experience at this hotel was excellent. The room we had was very large and comfortable. We decided not to spring for an ocean view room as we knew we wouldn't spend much time in the room. The beds were by far the best thing about the room. They were soooooo comfortable, I had an excellent restful sleep every night, which prepared me for all the activities we had packing into the day. The room was clean and nicely decorated, without feeling tacky. There was an enormous flat screen tv, which played Hawaii TV, which my family and I really enjoyed while in the room. The only negatives I would have about the room is that our bathroom could have been cleaner, and we did have a number of issues with our keys being deactivated. However, these are minor issues and the staff was very helpful when dealing with them. There is also a cost for internet access in your room however WiFi is free around the pool. The other major benefits to this hotel are its location and its amenities. The hotel is literally right across from Waikiki Beach, which cant be beat because there is no long trek to and from the beach. In fact, we never even went in the pool because the beach was so close! Also, the hotel restaurant, Tiki's had delicious food and drinks, friendly staff and was very reasonable. Also, the bottom level of the hotel has a conveniently located Wolfgang Puck Express and Cold Stone Creamery, both of which my family and I enjoyed and an ABC store around the corner. Lastly, I couldn't have more positive things to say about the staff. The front desk and housekeeping were always pleasant. We loved chatting with Dale at the poolside, we found Stacey at the Expedia desk very helpful when booking our rental car. Most of all, we couldn't say more about the Eric, the musician and the Hula dancer who accompanies him every morning at breakfast. The music and the dancing was a wonderful way to start everyday. The last day they even played a goodbye song to my family and I because we had become such fans and they taught us how to hula! The breakfast had a lot of variety and saved us alot of money on food!We fell in love with Hawaii and when we return it will certainly be to stay at the Resortquest Waikiki Beach Hotel! Mahalo! Mahalo! Mahalo!

<Author>bakphoenix
<Content>Great experience We took a shuttle from the airport and had driven through the not-so-nice areas of Honolulu and the parts of Waikiki Beach that were just shops and restaurants, but no beach. We hit a stretch of beach that was beautiful, and thought we had stopped in traffic, but a pleasant surprise was that we had arrived at our hotel, and we would be staying directly across the street from this great stretch of beach.The reception was very pleasant, the front desk gave us a warm and friendly reception, like they were truly glad to see us. They gave our child a welcome kit while we got the keys. It was nice to see all smiling faces after a long flight and a shuttle ride. The room was nice, colorful. The layout reveals it has been around a good number of years, but there was no sign of neglect in the room--all paint, furniture, wallpaper and carpeting were very fresh. The entire property was well-maintained. We got upgraded to a room that also had a great view of Diamond Head as well as an ocean view. Breakfast on the Beach was a nice concept...since the food is all meant to be grab-and-go if needed, it can't be quite as tailored as if it were to be served and eaten right there. The fruits and fresh juices were great. The hot items were nice to have, and for free, I was happy with them, but again, are mass-produced for people to eat later on that day, if they choose, so expectations should be adjusted to take that into consideration. Even if you didn't walk to the beach, you can sit poolside with an excellent ocean view. What a great way to enjoy some breakfast and morning coffee!Location...great! The best beach on Waikiki. Even my friends who live in Honolulu were impressed with the location. Waikiki itself is really a lot of stores and chain restaurants, so having the park on the other side really was nice.I found that the first time I was on the elevator, people were explaining to me how they worked, as I would later find out, they are a bit quirky, but most people found it had something of a charm. They seem to have minds of their own--if you don't put your key in fast enough (coming from the beach with your hands full makes it hard). Nothing awful, but unexpected. If you go to Honolulu, this place will help round out the experience nicely.

<Author>iburngb
<Content>Honeymoon trip It was our first trip to Hawaii. It was our honeymoon. It was the best time of our life...... ........ Well it started off great. We landed at about 12:00, had a limo waiting at baggage claim to give us beautiful leis. At the airport they were selling for about $50 +. The limo is a must if it is your first time visit. The only inconvenience is that if you want a rental car then you must find transportation from the hotel to the rental car facility. but it was not difficult at all. I believe the limo was around $133 round trip with leis. This was well worth it. ABC limousine was the company we used. I will definitely use them the next time, yes next time. With the limo we were allowed to sit back enjoy the scenery, give each other kisses then back to all the oh's and awhh's at all the beautiful things. No worries about directions, traffic, trying to sight see, etc...  We arrived at ResourtQuest Waikiki Beach hotel. From the outside it was nice. Nothing extreme but very pleasing. Checked in our luggage, then on up to the check in counter. This is where our first headache started. They first asked if we would stay in a downgraded room for two nights then they would upgraded us to better room than what we originally paid for (they overbooked the rooms). The only thing was it was from sister site down the street. They did say they would pay for a taxi. but really, we did not want to unpack for a couple of days then pack it up to move down the road. I do not think it was not that big of a upgrade. So i said no thanks. Well then they tell me they do not have the king bed i asked for. they only had twin beds. I told them that it was our honeymoon and that twin beds was not an option. well we went on for about 15 minutes they finally agreed that we would stay in the twin bed room for one day then they could move us to a room with a king bed. We gave in and said yes. well after we got in the room we thought if we were going to have to move to another room the next day we might as well take them up on there previous offer of the free upgrade, although in another hotel. Well needless to say, that offer no longer existed. oh well snooze you loose. Well our first room was nice. Small, but not too bad. Great view of Diamond head, probably one of the best views of it. Nice Hawaiian decor. We really could not complain except for the beds. The next day we went to our new room. it was on the other side of the hotel so we lost our Diamond Head view. But we gained a better view of the ocean. Much, Much better. Some may think of it as a downside others an upside. we were also right above the bar, and pool area. we thought of it as an benefit. we enjoyed opening the lanai and listening to the music, watching all the people dancing. it was nice to us. We could close the door and most all the music was drowned out. our first impressions of the hotel were good. The only thing is the overbooked of rooms and having to settle with a twin bed for one night. but you know crap happens and we were on top of the world, so it did not bother us that much. I mean a bed is a bed is a bed, if you know where i am coming from. We really enjoyed the breakfast experience. The food was uhhhhh, well so so. but the idea was amazing. It led us toward some great memories. In your room you have two small collapsible coolers. You use them for breakfast (or whatever you would like). You take your cooler downstairs and load it up with breakfast items that changes every other day. Either breakfast burritos, or sandwiches plus the fruits, cereal's, juices etc... We could and did take it down to the beach and eat it on a beach towel you can check out from the hotel. This created a memory we will never forget. Of course anyone can do this themselves but they make it easier for you. We went to the beach for breakfast twice, the rest of the times we took it back to our room and ate out on the lanai or ate in the car on the go.  Speaking of on the go we rented a car. We rented a sebring convertible. I would recommend a car. the reason for us it that we had reservations for shark diving one day, then swimming with dolphins another day. Then we went to Pearl Harbor, flea market at the stadium, PCC, a dinner cruise, North shore and more so we were very busy. We avoided the hassle of worrying about weather to get a taxi, the bus, what times the bus run. etc... We did use the bus though. Very nice and we would not need a car if we did not have so much planned and so much traveling the island. If we were (i mean when) return it is a high probability we would stay at this same hotel again. We liked it very well especially for its price. Sorry I can not remember the exact price. if you needed it i can find out just let me know. I did know that we stayed for 7 days 6 nights. We spent $5000. That was for airfare, hotel, PCC (upgraded Ambassador Luau package $118 each ) shark diving ($120 each), swimming with the dolphins ($199 each) limo ($133), rental car ($54 a day), and the eats, souvenirs, etc... So we did good with $5000. Over all we would recommend this hotel. 7.5 out of 10. Would been a 8 out of 10 if not for the bed mix-up.Enjoy your next trip,Mike

There was an ice machine outside our room. It was malfunctioning and made ice crunching noise every 30 minutes. Kinda irritating when your trying to sleep at night. I phoned the front desk and the maintenance folks fixed it for one night but it started up again. The complimentary breakfast was okay for our needs. They served cereal, pastries, bagels, yogurt, scrambled eggs, egg burritos, coffee, juice, fruit, miso soup, green noodles, and some rice triangles.The only negative thing about our vacation was that we had booked our trip through ResortQuest Reservation [--] and was told that every suite in the ResortQuest Waikiki Beach Hotel came with a microwave and coffee maker. This was not the case because none of the rooms in this hotel came with these amenities. So be warned, do not believe everything you hear when you phone the ResortQuest Reservation line. Best to phone the hotel directly for the correct information.

<Author>MNM7
<Content>Ok, but not impressed We stayed at this hotel for one night, prior to leaving for a cruise. The location is great, right on Waikiki beach. I had contacted the hotel prior to our stay to see if they offered shuttle service from the airport and to get info on Pearl Harbor tours. They recommended VIP shuttle, and said to contact the concierge desk when we arrived for tour info. Not really that much help, in my opinion.We did book transportation through VIP from the airport. There was a rep standing their with our name on a sign and transported our luggage to the shuttle. I thought that since there was a group of 8 that we'd have our own shuttle, but in reality we had to make two stops at other hotels before arriving to the ResortQuest. The cost was $10/each. The shuttle dropped us off at the curb and the bell services took our luggage. We went up one floor to check-in. That was pretty easy. We then went to the travel concierge, which was moreso a row of travel groups trying to sell tours. I was looking for unbiased info on what our options were, not a tour group trying to sell us something. So after being given a few brochures and being told to be back to book by 6:00, we made our way to our rooms.  The elevators were very slow, and confusing. The elevator system required us to enter our room key before we could enter the floor we needed. I know it's a security feature, but it was really more of a pain than anything. We got to the room to find the bellhop waiting with our luggage for his tip. The rooms are very small, surprisingly so. It also smelt like cigarette smoke, even though you had to sign an agreement acknowledging that the entire hotel is smoke free. But we figured it was one night no big deal. What bothered me most was the bathroom. For over $200 I expect the bathroom to be clean. The floors were filthy. And we couldn't believe there wasn't a fan in there! There really wasn't a good mirror to use when getting ready the next morning since the bathroom mirror was all fogged up.Like I said before, the best feature of the hotel is the location. We walked over to Waikiki beach and walked down the street to take in the scenery. The beds were pretty comfortable too, though full sized not queen. Our fellow travelers commented that the breakfast was very good. Unfortunately, our tour bus left for Pearl Harbor at 6:15, and breakfast did not start until 6:30. When we checked out we commented that they should start a little earlier. The lady checking us out was nice enough to flag down a staff member and they offered us the collapsible coolers that are provided for breakfast. I thought it was nice of them to do that, and those did come in handy on our cruise. They did have coffee available, and sodas. But it sounds like we missed out on the best feature fo the hotel, the breakfast. Overall, I wasn't very impressed with the hotel. I wouldn't run for the hills if you have a stay booked here and can't cahnge it. But I also wouldn't be too quick to recommend it. I expected more for the money.

If you are looking for a full breakfast buffet, this isn't it, but if you want to grab something quick to go that is delicious and filling, this is your place. They also had some miso soup and noodles as part of breakfast which were quite delicious. For the price, you are on the same street as some higher-priced properties but are able to enjoy the same location and nightlife and pay about 1/3 of the price. Looking at the map, I thought it would be too far away from everything else but it's about a 20 minute walk from one end of the beach to the other, so everything is very central. The gym was small but clean. They have 2 treadmills but why run indoors when you can run along Waikiki beach? The bathroom is small but the toiletries were quite nice. I had brought my own toiletries (you never know) but ended up not using them. Free wifi by the pool so if you bring your laptop you don't need to use the computers in the lobby. Lots of families at this hotel, I would highly recommend it!

The elevators in the hotel were really fast so you never really had to wait although you have to use your room card to use the elevator and sometimes it was a tad finicky. They have some computers there to use if you want to check out the internet etc. and some activity desks as well, we found them really nice and helpful. We didn't use the pool but it was a good size and it was nice having Tiki's bar and grill right there which is always a fun place to go to. All the staff were really nice and friendly. They usually have live music at Tikis at night so if you are a person that is looking for quiet this may not be the best hotel for you, it didn't bother us though and we enjoyed listening to the different bands etc. that played there. We stopped insome of the smaller towns around the island and asked the locals aboutthe best spots to hit. Everyone we stopped and talked to was so friendly. We ventured to theBig Island, and visited the volcano, make sure you don't have any respiratory issues prior to visiting because it will wear you out withall the sulphur in the air. We then visted the black sand beach and got our own sea turtle encounter. There were three just hanging out inthe cove. How fun! The next day we went to Hanauma Bay, It was so beautiful, the fish were everywhere and we even got to swim next to a sea turtle there as well. NOTE: It's worth renting a car for the duration of the trip. Hanauma bay is $5 a person and all you need to do is go to Walmart, buy a bag,snorkle gear and some beach mats. It's worth the savings if you have a family with you.That evening we went on a delightful catamaran ride with the Makani. Its an amazing machine. Capt. Jon was filled with stories and information about the island he was so friendly we stayed on the Captains deck for the duration of the trip. If you are military, catch a show at Blaizdel theater for Rush seating. We saw The Lion King for a discounted price of $33. The regular price was $86. The theater had horribly uncomfortable seats, but the show was amazing.Pearl Harbor was amazing, we were actually there on Veterans Day. The tour we selected was inclusive of the Bowfin/Arizona/Missouri. When on the Missouri try to find the tour guuide who actually worked on the Missouri during its involvement in WWII. He was filled with funny stories. Again military discount applied here and made a huge difference.Overall it was a great trip and I would stay at the ResortQuest Waikiki Beach Hotel, gpod price, breakfast was OK. We will be returning next year!

<Author>T_Norton
<Content>Nice Hotel. Great Location! My husband and I stayed at the ResortQuest Waikiki Beach for our 2 year anniversary. Upon arrival, the ground floor of the hotel is really inviting. You have to take an elevator/escalator to get to the hotel lobby to check in, but we didn't find that too troubling.The hotel room is really small (as other reviewers have indicated), so for persons traveling with a large group or families traveling with children, I would not recommend this hotel, particularly if there are more than two people in your party. The same can be said for the hotel bathroom. It's rather small, and not the best in terms of cleanliness, but it serves its purpose. Hotel towels are plentiful, as well as all of the other usual amenities. The hotel is directly across the street from the Marriott, which is nice and the location is great! With a short walk across the street, you'll find yourself on Waikiki Beach. Also, for convenience there areseveral food establishments directly downstairs on the ground floor--particularly, Wolfgang Puck's Express, Coldstone Creamery, and Subway just to name a few. Other than that, there aren't too many (fast) food places nearby. There's Teddy Burger, which is a short walk around the corner, but if you're looking for a McDonald's, Burger King, etc. you'll have to walk several blocks to find one. Either way, the food prices in Hawaii are somewhat expensive, so your selection really won't matter price wise. A typical hamburger, french fries, and beverage meal will run you close to, if not more than $10. Here's a food tip!!! ABC Pharmacy, which is pretty much on every corner in Honolulu has these great hot dogs for $0.99, They're pretty good, plus you can grab one on the go. This place is also good for some of your souveneir and beverage options.Other than the location and dining options, I found the hotel to be relatively average. Their state of the art security system requires that you use your room key to go up on the elevator which can become a pain, but better safe than sorry. One gripe is that when my husband and I got up in the middle of the night (around 4 am) to see if we could find something to eat, the elevators were not fully operational. We waited approx. 15-20 minutes for the elevator to come to our floor, along with others who were waiting with their luggage and decided to try the stairs (from the 15th floor)! As many of the other reviewers mentioned, their FREE morning breakfast offering gives this hotel an advantage, BUT if you're a meat eater this is not the place for you. The breakfast is mainly continental, with one or two added selections, but don't look for much more. It's very filling and serves its purpose, plus you can get as much as you like! Some of the selections are rather atypical, but chalk it up to experiencing something new. Oh, and unless you're looking to break the bank, I would not recommend the hotel restaurant, Tiki's. It's rather pricey, and I'd say that you could find several other good restaurants within a short walking distance for about the same price, or much less.The hotel pool was small and a few people used it or sat out on the patio and tanned, but if you'omplaining about the hotel pool, why in the heck did you go to Waikiki, which is known for its beach? Other than that, I'd say the hotel is just about average. Nothing to write home about, but nothing to gripe about either. It has several advantages in terms on convenience and proximity to food and fun. Besides, who goes to Hawaii to stay in the hotel room anyway. Overall, I'd say it's a good place to stay and I'd probably stay there again.

<Author>Waikiki6
<Content>Good hotel for location and price I stayed the week of Sept 11-18 2007. I was vacationing alone. I booked a partial ocean view and waited (held out) until I got the king bed I'd requested. I was offered a 2-bed room hours before, at check in, but waited until I got what I wanted for the week - and it only took a few more hours.The room was on the 8th floor, at the back of the hotel - but not on the Diamond Head side. I had an ok view, but since it was lower, there were trees in the way. Again, the view was ok, and if I'd wanted to spend more, I would have probably booked ocean-front. Ocean views would have probably been a bit better but I was worried about being over the bar after reading previous reviews, and didn't want to deal with any possible excess noise. I booked thru a travel agent that uses a larger company that specilizes in Hawaiian holidays. The rate was average. I asked if there were any possible upgrades, but the hotel was completely booked. The Air Force was celebrating 60 years, and the Aloha Festivals were begining as well. The room was clean and the housekeeping service was excellent. I never needed to have anything corrected. I used a bag they provided to go down 4 mornings to get breakfast. They provided bagles, pastry, coffee, tea, fresh cut fruit, yogurt, cereal, milk and every day had a warm selection as well, usually something like a breakfast burrito: scrambled egg, sausage meat, rolled into a tortilla, or a small square of quiche of egg, meat and perhaps cheese. Oh - and I prepared in advance and packed a coffee thermos holder (16-20 ounce) from Starbucks that was thermal so that I could fill it each morning and it would remain hot for several hours. There is also a Starbucks on the corner where you could purchase one if you're a coffee drinker and want it for free each morning. The Hotel has a Wolfgang Puck Express on the street level which offers a variety of pizza, sandwitches, soups, pasta and salads, and you can get them to go. The Tiki's restaurant and bar has a lunch and dinner menu, (which you can find online), and I found their selections to be good as well. You will also find a Subway sandwitch shop, a cookie shop and an ABC store all on premises or at the end of the block. The ABC stores now provide the free service of blowing up flotation devices like the $1.99 air mattress, as well as trinkets, snacks, spirits, mixer etc. I used the gym a couple of times...it's small but there are several cardio machines and some free weights and it was usually empty. Sat out at the pool several times, which was generally quiet and always found a lounge chair. It is at one end of Waikiki, but more quiet than staying right in the middle of the stretch. Get up early 5:30 - 6am and go for a brisk walk on the waterfront, it's quiet and good exercise. You can walk all the way down to the Hilton Hawaiian and back in about 45 minutes, either going on the beach or the sidewalk, depending on how fast you walk.Yes, there are homeless about, generally more than you would see at the other end, but generaly they don't bother anyone. I only saw a time or two when they would ask for a smoke or a bit of spare change, but you can truly assist or ignore, they don't pester....they just ask someone else. I didn't have a problem with the elevators once I figured out to have my room card at the ready upon entering the lift.

<Author>highlandbride
<Content>Room 1126 - noisy, but great view of Diamond Head This is our third trip to Waikiki, and our second time staying at this hotel. It's been redecorated and upgraded a bit since our last stay which is nice. Better beds, flat panel TVs, better carpeting, but the walls are still thin (this is an adjoining room so we heard our neighbor's phone calls, kids crying etc) and the lines for the elevators are still frustrating. Prior to getting into room 1126 we spent one very loud night in room 511 which is one floor above the pool and the bar. Unless you want to hear all the noise and watch all the pool action, including the breakfast crowd that starts to gather at 6:30am, don't accept any odd numbered rooms below the 9th floor.The included breakfast was starch heavy and erratic. So much for serving breakfast until 9:30 - if you don't get down to the breakfast area by the pool (including Hawaiian singer and hula dancer) by 8:15 AM it's picked clean. Not good for those who don't eat dairy or have issues with gluten. Better - visit the bar at Tiki's in the hotel for a nightcap and your receipt will likely include a two for one breakfast offer for the full buffet at Tikis the next morning. $12.99 for two for a real breakfast is still good value.We took the free trolley to Hilo Hatties to do some shopping and spotted Sam Choy's restaurant one block from the store. So, save yourself a stiff taxi ride and hit Hilo Hattie's and Sam Choy's for lunch one day during your stay. Just make sure to get your shell lei from the greeters at the store so you can get a free ride back to Waikiki. Sam Choy's serves excellent Hawaiian food and seafood. A little bit more than some places but the portions are huge and can be split between two adults with pretty good appetites.

<Content>Okay Place, beware of the valet service We reserved our trip through Costco.com with the hopes that this would be a decent place to stay in Waikiki. Tiki's grill is okay, but I thought it was very overpriced for what you got. We had dinner one night on the beach at Duke's where the food was much better, service was outstanding, and the bill was much less than Tiki's. For anyone going to Waikiki I reccommend making a reservation at Duke's at least one night. Now for the downside of this hotel. The housekeeping forgot to clean our room one day, but when I called front desk they brought towels right away and it didn't happen again. I really thought it was very stingy not to provide wireless internet for free, the parking was awful, the valet's were rude, and I had my GPS stolen from my car because when you pull up they rush you so much that you don't have time to make sure you have everything, and all this for a whopping $20 a DAY!!!! I really don't appretiate the fact that the valet's take advantage of the We are not responsible for lost or stolen items clause on the claim ticket!! Resortquest, you need to run better background checks on your parking staff, and maybe teach them how to be a little more polite to the guests who are paying $20 a day to park there and then another $300 a day to sleep!Anyways, enough ranting...I would suggest this hotel to families and make sure to get a room on the upper floors on the Diamond Head side. I heard some of the guests complaining that the music from Tiki's will keep you up all night and into the morning on the pool side of the hotel. The elevators weren't as bad as in other reviews, for us anyways. We would probably not stay here again, or anywhere in Waikiki for that matter. Last time we visited Oahu we stayed in a vacation rental in Kailua which was by far the best part of the whole island. Once you pay for the accomodations there is no extra charge for parking, most units have washers and dryers and meals are much more affordable since you have a kitchen to cook in or a BBQ to use. The beaches in Kailua are the best in Hawaii as well. So for anyone staying at the Resortquest Waikiki Beach, just beware of the parking situation, don't let the valets rush you, and the rest of your stay should be great.

<Content>THE Best Hotel in Waikiki By a Long Shot My husband, myself and our 23 month old daughter stayed at the ResortQuest Waikiki Beach Hotel for ten days. We had front row seats to the bluest ocean you could ever imagine and also the best of Waikiki's beachfront skyline at night!! I could not even imagine that any of the so-called 'absolute beachfront' hotels could be any better than this. It is THE place to stay on the whole of Waikiki Beach. We took our breakfast back to our room and sat on our 'ocean front' balcony, the best seat anywhere!! Breakfast was available from 6.30 to 9.30am each day. We always collected ours around 8.30am and there was always plenty to go around. The hotel room was awesome! It was plenty big enough for the three of us. The bathroom was not 'tiny' like a lot of people mention. It was a pretty standard size bathroom from what I have experienced. Plenty of cupboard space for your luggage. A flat screen tv was a nice extra. The decor was really modern and funky. Our king size bed was the most comfortable bed I have ever slept on. I cannot praise the staff more highly. We were treated like royalty from the moment we checked-in. Everyone was so friendly and courteous and attended to our requests efficiently. The ONLY negative thing I can think of is, yes, the lifts can be quite slow at times. But what can you expect from a hotel that EVERYBODY wants to be at and you are all trying to get to your rooms during peak times. Have a little patience people and chill out!! You are on vacation!! We will absolutely, most definitely stay at the ResortQuest Waikiki Beach Hotel the next time we stay on Oahu. No questions asked!!
