<Author>suspision
<Content>Hanging Loose at Resortquest Waikiki Beach We stayed at the Resortquest Waikiki Beach Hotel. The hotel was an overall great choice, great location not far from anything at all, all the shuttles/trolley stop at the hotel. The decor is funky and cute, the beds were sooooo comfortable, plenty of pillows, comfortable down comforter and sheets. Room size was adequate, the A/C worked fine, not too noisy at all. We had a partial ocean view with double beds on the 11th floor. The lanai was small but it has wonderful views of diamond head and the beach/ocean (more than expected). It was not as noisy as read on past reviews. At around two or three, the restaurants do throw away their trash and that's the only noise we heard and it was quick, no more than five minutes of noise. The walls are not as thin as we read, we barely heard other people sneeze or hurl. The only thing that could use improvement in the room was the bathroom. There was adequate amount of counterspace for toiletries, the hair dryer and makeup mirror were nice to have, but the bathtub had some kinks to it. The shower curtain was on round rod which gave you plenty of space to shower but there was no way to adjust the water pressure and the bath tub would flood easily because water came out too fast! The hallway was always clean and there was no strange odors. The elevators were generally fast. The only times they would not come fast was when there was free breakfast rushhour which was at 9:00 am when the breakfast was almost over and people were either rushing to get their breakfast before it finished or when people would take their breakfast to the room. But at other times of the day or night the elevators worked fine and were pretty fast. The hotel does have 25+ floors so its understandable. Only once our room was not cleaned but when we reported it they came and cleaned it promptly. The safe is a ripoff, just hide stuff in you luggage. Breakfast was not superb but it was good for coffee, fruit, milk, tea, OJ, Sodas, pastries/bagels and of course all you can eat cereal!!! Parking was expensive but it was convenient to park there as it was close and one can call to request the car, every minute counted, no time to waste to pick up the car from far away. Tiki's Grill and Bar was excellent! Try the Lava Flow here, best on the Island. Cold Stone's is good but much more expensive than on the mainland. Next door Hula's has good food at a good price, the service needs improvement. Duke's has a good reputation, but our steaks were charred even when we sent them back! Too much money to get it wrong, even sizzler gets it right! The Royal Hawaiian has the best Mai Tai's on the Island! Try the Chi Chi also, or the Blue Hawaii you might like those drinks. Try their Luau, there are several reasons to go. 1) its close by (you could walk there) 2) its not too many people 3) the food is good 4)you could get a coupon online for it 20% discount 5) it lets you out at 8:30 pm and you could get some more shopping done across the street! Renting a car was a great idea, Alamo rates are cheaper if you book online and they have a free shuttle to pick you up and drop you off. The cleanliness of the cars are not that good but it was cheap for a convertible! Go around the whole island and explore it! Try Leonards malasadas on Kapahulu about a mile from Waikiki. BikeHawaii.com guide was the sweetest person, ask Jeremy for good advice on places to eat o to do if you book an activity with them!

The hotel did not do a good job of getting everyone together to inform us of what was happening , and there seemed to be no management plans in action to handle this kind of natural disaster. We discovered this was Hawaii's first major quake in 30 years... just our luck. Equally unlucky for us was being on the 17th floor. We had been eating breakfast when the hotel started to shake at around 7am . As the lifts were out with loss of power we had to trek up the stairs to get money and stuff from our room.Our hotel having the breakfast on the beach cool bags was one of the few able to still feed its residents during this time.. this we were grateful for. We saw many people lining up outside the islands many ABC stores trying to buy supplies during our day but our hotel was fantastic and let everyone take out as many food items as they wanted that day. For this reason alone I would stay at this hotel again. The rooms have recently been refurbished and have 42inch plasma Tv's ,comfy beds and decent storage for anyone staying a couple of weeks. In Oahu you'd not really be spending much time in your room anyway there is plenty to do .

You could hook up to internet in the room for an additional cost, but if you have wireless, you just take your lap top down to the pool deck and use it for free. The only wireless hot spot is on the pool deck. Our favourite restaurants were the 2 at the hotel, Tiki's and Wolfgang Puck's. The meals were delicious and quite reasonable in price. The service was fast as well. All the staff at the hotel was very friendly and accomodating. If you called for housekeeping or bell service, they were there immediately.The cooler bag breakfast was great and we could always pack enough for lunch and put it in the fridge in our room. Having to buy only one meal a day really was a saving. We tried Cheeseburger in Paradise, but were not impressed. Also, avoid Planet Hollywood. That was the worst meal we had. We had the early bird special at Chuck's Steakhouse at the Outrigger and it was very good. We did the 2 for 1 luau that comes with the package and the show was excellent. Be sure to go early to get a good seat. When the hotel advertises that kids stay and eat free, it is a bit of a misnomer. The kids eat free at 2 or 3 restaurants that are not at all close to the hotel. They do not eat free at the hotel restaurants. However, with free breakfast and lunch for everyone, this was not a real concern. The kids loved the International Marketplace and we visited it several times. It is about a 10 minute walk. They also loved the beach because there were always waves to ride. Take water shoes, because there are some stones and rocks in the ocean. We loved this hotel and we would go back in a minute!

Late check out cost us $60. But it was like having an extra day, we drove to a beach, hung out, swam, ate dinner, and got to come back for showers and finish packing. a great deal I thought. We will definitely stay here next time we come to Waikiki!

<Author>sunbird1
<Content>Had to sign a no-smoking agreement at check-in When we booked this we were aware of their non-smoking policy - Hawaiian law prohibits smoking in public buildings. However, most hotels will allow smoking on the balcony of your room (as our friendsat the Marriott next door did). My fault for not calling and asking if it was permitted on the balcony. At check-in, we had to sign a waiver saying that if we were caught smoking, we'd be charged a $450.00 penalty by the hotel. Resortquest should post this info on their website. If you smoked, you had to go outside of the building - even in the open-air areas, it was not allowed. Had we known this, we would not have stayed there. The main reason we booked this hotel was their breakfast-on-the-beach - it sounded so charming. There are individual soft-side coolers in your room. You take it poolside where the breakfast buffet is held each morning from 7 - 10. You fill your cooler and off you go to the beach or you can sit at one of the tables, or take it back to your room. The selection was good but several mornings they ran out of fresh fruit by 8 am. Great Kona coffee, though. Their restaurant, Tiki, is very good. If you go, try the macademia nut encrusted mahi. Excellent. Also there is a Wolfgang Puck express on site that offers great rosemary chicken. Changed rooms three times in 7 days - the first was a king and we'd booked two doubles; the second room was over the bar  lounge (noisy) and the third had a problem with the a/c but we kept it anyway because it had a great view of Diamond Head. Saw lots of both couples and families and they all looked like they were having a good time.The pool is next to the open-air lounge and closes at 8 PM - just about the time I was ready for a dip after a long day of sight-seeing. Shucks!

<Author>dreamonixx
<Content>Be here - now Ok just so you know who I am here goes. I am a long haul flight attendant with a premium international airline. I stay in over 110 rooms a year and then there are my vacation times - so, well over 130 nights a year. I expect quality and most of all SERVICE. This hotel has blown me away TOTALLY. I usually have things which irritate me or make me lean toward a bad review however NOT HERE. The things which do irritate me are other reviewers who have given this property a bad wrap, usually over the breakfast offering. So when you check in they give each guest a little cooler bag and each morning you go down by the pool and fill it with an assortment of cereals, fresh fruit, hot food and bakery items. Coffee, tea, juice and fresh milk is also available there. This is meant to be a light breakfast - not a Vegas buffet. You can take your cooler bag and sit on the beach or do what we did and sit by the pool, listen to the Hawaiian music and watch the Hula dancer. I realised that Americans perceive quality as SIZE rather than content so maybe this is why they moan about the LIGHT breakfast. If you want the big heart attack on a plate meals go somewhere else because this isn't for you. Anyway, back to the hotel itself. At check in a woman offered us juice as we waited in the line to check in. At the desk nothing was too much trouble and once we got to the room we were delighted. Great views and clean, fresh facilities. EVERY MEMEBER OF STAFF WE ENCOUNTERED BEHAVED LIKE AN OWNER OF THE COMPANY and took pride in their job. NOTHING was ever too much trouble. Quite frankly there is no where else to stay in Waikiki so stop looking immediately.

Our second night we upgraded to an oceanfront room which I highly recommend doing. The view was breathtaking, and we spent our early evenings just sitting on our balcony sipping on cocktails and taking in the sites. The restaurant/bar, Tiki's, had good food and an awesome view as well. All in all, we loved our stay at the ResortQuest Waikiki Beach Hotel, and we would absolutely stay there again the next time we make it to Honolulu. If the pool stayed open a little bit later (it closes at 7pm), I would have rated our experience as a perfect 10 as far as location, accommodations, and value.

<Author>fijisunsets
<Content>Fantastic Stay Dates stayed : April 15 - April 20, 2007My sister and I just returned from Honolulu where we stayed at the Resort Quest Waikiki Beach Hotel. If you want a hotel close to the action but away from the hustle and bustle, this is it. The hotel is ideally located across the street from the beach and within walking distance of all the shops, restaurants, etc that the Waikiki Beach area offers. We booked a package that included the Breakfast on the Beach offer. What a fun concept that is. We each were provided a small insulated cooler that we would fill with our breakfast. Each morning there was all you could eat cereal, small sweet rolls, some type of breakfast sandwich with meat and egg, fruit, juices, milk, tea, soft drinks, wonderful Kona coffee. This was a fantastic deal considering the price of breakfast in Honolulu. Plus there was a singer and hula dancer every morning, which made breakfast very special. In fact, there was live music pretty much all during the afternoon and evening which was a nice touch.The hotel has a restaurant called Tikis which had great food. The lava flow desert was awesome. I found the prices here a bit cheaper than most of the places we ate. The service was friendly and it was a popular place each evening on the patio, which overlooked the beach and beautiful sunsets. The rooms are decorated very Hawaiian-ish and I found it charming. The beds were the most comfortable I have even felt in a hotel. There were great bath amenities. We had a refrigerator, iron and ironing board, and a small safe. There was a small lanai and our room was an ocean view, so we sat on the lanai most evenings to listen to the waves and people watch. The staff at the hotel was awesome. The pool area staff was the best. In the pool area, there was a soda fountain and canned sodas and the prices were very inexpensive. Here you could check out a beach towel for the day. The hotel offered several activity desks, internet acccess, valet parking (if you rent a car) and a small sundry shop. I could go on and on but if you want a very nice quiet hotel, with awesome views, awesome staff the Resort Quest Waikiki Beach Hotel is the one for youLucy N

<Author>westcoastgirrl
<Content>Great for Families! After much research I decided to book our 8 night stay in Waikiki at this hotel. I was very pleased and everything was as expected. We paid $213 per night with one night free for a partial ocean view. The room was updated with an LCD TV, new carpet. I travelled with my husband and 2 small children (1  4) and with my inlaws. I booked adjoining rooms and both were ready when we arrived around 1pm. The down side was we would have liked one room with 2 beds and 1 with a king, but all they could do was give us 2 beds in each room. Unfortunately they were double beds not queens which we are used to. We gave our luggage to the bell desk and our car was parked. Valet is mandatory and $20US per day which I think is very pricey, but all expected. The bell desk did not get our luggage to us for about 3 hours which was very annoying as we had alot and were still in our Vancouver weather clothing. Our rooms were on the 18th floor and had an awesome view of Diamond Head! The lanai was very small though and no chairs or space to sit out on the lanai. I think rooms facing other directions have chairs. The room was small for the 4 of us but the amenities of the area were great. I liked being near the quieter end of waikiki strip and across the road from the beach. This end is sheltered from large waves by a wall and is perfect if you have small children. We enjoyed the complimentary self serve breakfast each morning also. Each room has 2 cooler bags that you take down to the pool area and fill with items. It was usually the same stuff - individual cereals, yogourt, miso soup, rice, mini muffins, mini bagels, a pastry, fresh fruit containers (local fruit), coffee, juices and a hot selection - which was usually not good - tater tots, scrambled egg on a bagel, french toast sticks. Some ordinary bread with a toaster was not available and would have been nice but we made do. We usually took extra cereal or muffins for the kids to snack on later. I do not think all rooms come with breakfast though - and this seems to be contrary to ResortQuests website. We had yellow room cards which we needed to show to get into breakfast. Some people had red ones and I overheard the man saying that breakfast is $10 for them (not worth $10!). We had partial ocean view rooms so maybe standard don't get it. Check beforehand! The rooms have mini fridges which come in handy. (The in room safe is also $3 per day). I found the gift shop in the parking level well priced for souvenirs and the ABC store on the corner had everything. It was actually a bit better priced than other ABC's (maybe because its at the end of the strip). TIki's restaurant by the pool is excellent for lunch and has the best pina coladas I found. Cold Stone Creamery is awesome too. The ice cream is mixed together while you watch with whatever you want in it (ie for brownies - they cut them up and add them right there) - HUGE portions though! I was a bit disappointed in the ResortQuest Kids Play, Stay  Eat free program though. At check-in I received a bag with buckets  shovels, coloring book  crayons and each child got a card. The kids meals are not free at the on-site restaurant (Tiki's) and the only place we took advantage of this was 1 night for ribs at Tony Romas. I think the other restaurant was Sizzler? Not much anyway. When we went to the PCC they said we needed the coupon from the book given at check in for the kids to get in free - which I didn't bring (only the card) but they waived the coupon thank goodess. When I returned to the room  re-read the book it did indeed say to just show the card..I don't know - I'd just bring the book anyway. The program did offer alot of free attractions for kids though. Sorry such a long review - but I did really enjoy this hotel and would definitley stay here again. It is one of the best priced and you can't beat being at the beach. Its definitely a family property and if it were just me and my husband I'd probably consider something more central  fancier (like the Sheraton).

So over all my only complaint was the valet in the fact that we are not use to it and the feeling of being obligated to tip. Ex if we went out we had to make sure we had everything we needed an once we left the hotel we left the hotel and tried not to comeback until we were done. I liked the in and out convenience without the valet though. Over all I would recommend this hotel, it was one of the modern ones and it had a gym which was nice. I may not go back to this hotel only because of valet. I like being able to come and go as I please w/o having to call for my car and paying every time I call and drop off my car. If you do not have an issue with valet go to this hotel. It is one of the better ones.

<Author>emah
<Content>generally fine, but a few reservations I stayed at the Waikiki Beach Hotel from Dec 29 through Jan 4 2007. I had a small room on the 6th floor (603) and overall am happy with my experience. I looked around for ages to find a decent but affordable hotel on waikiki beach, and read the reviews with some concern but I think, for me, this was a good choice. First the room: I decided not to pay for an ocean view but in fact pretty much all of the rooms in this hotel have a view anyway from the Lanai. Outside my balcony is the Marriott, but the view of the water is fine when standing outside. the absolute most important thing to me in a hotel is the bed - usually i pay for the sheraton for this reason but the price on waikiki is outrageous. anyway, this bed is easily as comfortable as the sheraton bed. a lovely pillowtop cover, firm, and high off the ground, lots of pillows, good quality bedding - just perfect and more than makes up for the shortcomings of the room. there is also an enormous plasma screen tv - 1 metre across x 60cms deep. amazing.there is a small barfridge and the room safe is big enough for my laptop and everything else. the bathroom is small but well organised - someone else complained here about the curved shower rail but in fact it is great - there is an inner curtain to stop water dripping over the edge of the bathtub and the curve means you have plenty of room to manouver without getting stuck to the curtain. toiletries are ok. the couple of maintenance issues i had were dealt with very promptly (I did as somone here suggested and had them override the AC system so that it does not turn off at night, and they also helped me set up my laptop so i can tune into the internet here in the US. the room itself is very small but i expected that, as the frommers guide made much of the small rooms. for one person it was perfectly ok, even though my room is a disaster zone with all the shopping spread out on every available space. i had lunch one day at the tiki grill and that staff were very attentive and helpful and service was fast. although they don't really do vegetarian food at all, they made me a sandwich on request. the bad: the staff are friendly but not very helpful. yesterday i was given completely contradictory and incorrect information that stuffed up my day; i strongly recommend that you call the tour companies or look up shuttle schedules on the internet yourself - they don't really instill a great deal confidence when it comes to information about tourism activities or even cabs - both times i asked the bellboy to call me a cab i ended up going on to the street and waving one down myself - faster!they charge $3 a day for the inroom safe which i think is really nickle and dime stuff - it should be included in the room charge. they also charge $10 a day for the internet which strikes me as pretty excessive but maybe that it just because i am used to having it for free. using a phone card incurs the same costs as making a domestic call anyway which is irritating, the buffet breakfast which they rave about is really pretty dreadful. and the bad thing is, that its here so its hard to make yourself go elsewhere and have something decent. there seems to be a two-day rotation for the hot stuff (which is really yech - french toast strips or potato gems, all soft and greasy - and something with egg and meat which they cut up into squares and either stick in a muffin or in a box - stay clear. but there is cereal and yoghurt and pieces of fresh fruit which it is hard to muck up, lots of coffee and juice, and those mini bagels with jelly which people seem to like, after day two its all very uninspiring. the other negative is location. while it is true that the hotel is literally across the street from the beach, unless you have a child and want to spend all day playing in the shallow ocean pool they have created, you have to walk at least 500 metres to get past the pool and the barriers, to get to free ocean. its not a big drag or anything but it is a little misleading. next time i would try out the waikiki circle hotel which is literally opposite the first place you can actually free swim.so; overall satisfied, but not without some reservations.

This creates two problems: 1) when you're sleeping at night, motionless, your A/C goes off and the room gets hot, and 2) after a long day in the heat, it feels good to come back to a cool room, but it would be hot because the thermostat would shut off while we were gone. This CAN be resolved. Simply call the front desk and they will send someone up to override the setting on your thermostat.

I would consider the breakfast continental style - they gave you small cooler bags to pack your breakfast and go (probably not a good idea - people would pack these bags with way more food than they would eat, allowing some items to run out before the breakfast was over). The entire staff was friendly and helpful, including the parking staff at the valet. We never had to wait for our car, we would call from our room and by the time we were down in 15 minutes, it would be waiting ($15 is what they charge per night, which is reasonable for parking in waikiki). The hotel also allowed us to do a late checkout which good since many flights back to the mainland leave in the late afternoon or evening (must request the day of your departure and the hotel will charge you if it is 2pm or later). My favorite part of the hotel was the restraunt Tiki's. We made reservations one evening and were set overlooking the beach. They have a great menu, the food was delicious, and the staff so friendly. We booked our room through resortquest website and got the 4th night free (great deal).

<Author>1TheIceman1
<Content>If something goes wrong during your stay, BEWARE We stayed at this hotel for six nights at the end of October for our Honeymoon. We intended to save a few dollars by staying here and really regretted this decision. The few perks offered to honeymoon couples is that they provide you with a complimentary upgrade from a garden view to an ocean facing room. They also give you a bottle of champagne. Here is the story on the rooms: The garden rooms face another hotel that is approximately 15 stories high. If your room is on the right side of the hotel you will be looking directly into another hotel. The ocean facing rooms have a decent view, however, the rooms are exremely loud in that the face busy Kalukala Ave, and an adjacent street. Be prepared for early mornings sounds of buses, garbage trucks, and delivery trucks backing up (beep, beep, beep) into the delivery entrance of the Marriott next door that happens to face this hotel. The lower your floor is the louder it is going to be. There is a bar called Tikis which plays live music during breakfast and at night. You can clearly hear this music if you are staying in a room below floor 10 that faces the ocean. Don't expect large rooms; they are tiny. If you are travelling for a few weeks like we did, you will have space issues with all of your bags. Apparently they updated about half of their rooms: a cheap LCD tv, new paint, and new furniture. Lipstick on a pig. This is a old hotel and you can see through this. The pool here is atrocious. It gets absolutely no sun, is extremely small and serves little purpose other than providing a nice backdrop. The parking situation is bad. Real bad. You have no choice but to valet your car, it costs $15 and takes apporximately 10-15 minutes for them to retireve your car. We found it inconvenient to have to ask a valet to fetch our car, wait, and then be expected to tip him afterwards. Although we returned our car the hotel attempted to charge us for two nights of valet parking that we never used. Kind of hard since we had no car to park. Make sure to read your itemized bill at check out!!!! Breakfast is included with your room. A nice way to save a few dollars, they do change the menu every other day, but it does get old real quick. My advice is to grab a few coffees and head elsewhere for breakfast. They serve a pretty unhealthy mixture of food, ranging from egg sandwiches to tater tots. Here is the nightmare. We were upgraded from a garden room to an ocean facing room Room 725 on the 7th floor. Our first night there was a bad night since the live band was playing at Tiki's below. They 7th floor is only 3 levels above the terrace area for Tikis so you hear people talk, scream, and every note from the band. You won't get a good night sleep on a low floor at this hotel. The A/C in this room stopped working one night when we were getting ready for dinner. We also noticed that the A/C unit which was housed in the bathroom ceiling was leaking. We called maintenance and they soon opened the ceiling panel which dumped 5-6 gallons of water all over our bathroom thereby ruining our toiletries. (We were compensated $25 and had to go to the ABC store to purchase new tooth brushes, etc.) After speaking to the manager, his name was Joe the night manager, he struggled to give me apology and said he would move us to a new room. Think about how horrible it is to have to re-pack everything you had already unpacked and leave the room while trying not to leave anything behind. This all happened during dinner time: we were starving and missed our dinner reservation. We then moved to Room 2111. Laying in bed, I could not help notice a constant crashing noise that would rattle the walls and light fixures in our room. After investigating a little more, I discovered that Joe the manager had placed us in a room directly next to a bank of three elevators. It pains me to think that he had the audactiy to move us to that awful room after the first expereince with the noise and bad A/C unit. I then went to the front desk at 12:30 am and spoke with the manager again. He was completely clueless as to the situation and didn't bother to utter on apology. He then promised a new room in the morning. After checking with the front desk in the morning about our new room, we were informed that we would have to empty all of our belongings from the old room 2111 by 12:00pm in order to move. After a short argument, we refused and went on our way. This hotel again had the audacity to try to uproot us for their own convenience and had no idea what they were putting us through. So after re-packing again, we were moved to Room 2519. Great view, the A/C worked, and it was quiet. Finally no problems here, but after that whole ordeal we vowed to never give any business to this hotel chain again. Lesson learned: Do not stay here. If something goes wrong here, and it will, the staff is incapable of providing a bare minimum level of customer service and cannot solve simple problems.

<Author>cksiam
<Content>Very pleased with our stay here! My wife and I just returned from our stay at this hotel in Waikiki. My first time in Hawaii (my wife's third). Before booking, I looked at many reviews and decided on the Waikiki Beach hotel. I am VERY happy that we stayed here. Here's a quick rundown on the various features/issue other reviewers have praised or criticized:ROOM SIZES and VIEW: Yes, the rooms are small as are the bathrooms, but they are hardly as cramped as some make them out to be. To keep things in perspective, my brother-in-law from Japan was staying at the Sheraton Waikiki and his room directly faced the beach. Aside from the slightly fancier bathroom, his room was no bigger than our own (seriously). In fact, I found our rooms to be much more pleasant. Okay, so his balcony was much larger. While we had a Partial Ocean View room (on the Diamond Head side), we had to go out on the balcony to see the ocean. Nothing great and may not even be worth paying for unless you feel you must spend time out on the balcony. BUT from our beds we had a direct view of Diamond Head. Fortunately, that view from our room wasn't blocked by the adjacent hotel (rooms on the same side but closer to the beach would be looking directly at the other hotel). Not sure what the view on the otherside of the hotel would look like, but the side we were on was very quiet (because a street wasn't directly below us). Overall, anyone who is not a spoiled princess/prince will find the room size perfectly comfortable for two people (with two small kids, it would get cramped as most non-suite rooms would). As for the view, truthfully, without the direct Diamond Head view, the POV would be nothing special. BEDS: Very, very comfortable. We slept very well.ELEVATORS: We stayed on the 12th floor and really couldn't tell what people were complaining about. Perhaps the elevators were part of the recent renovations. The elevators were fine.CLIMATE CONTROLS in Room: Worked great. Quiet too. The hallways and elevators did not seem to be as well ventilated/cooled as they could have been, though. Who knows why? None-the-less, this wasn't an issue at all. Everything was clean, well maintained and nothing smelled.BREAKFAST ON THE BEACH: Excellent. The food was good (not great), but enough variety. My wife is Japanese and she enjoyed the Japanese food they had very much. Fresh fruit, cereal, changing egg items (sandwiches, omelettes, etc.), french toast, mini-bagels, muffins, coffee. Sometimes we would eat in the morning, and pack muffins, fruit, etc with us for lunch on days we were just hanging out at the beach. It was really convenient, especially when we went snorkeling at Hanauma Bay. Also, they have a hula dancer and singer/guitar player from 8:00 to 9:30 AM. Very nice to have breakfast on the pool deck and outside Tikis in the morning overlooking the beach and listening to the music.SERVICE: Very nice. Casual, too. Not fancy-smancy as my grandmother would say.TIKIS: We ate there several times. The food wasn't spectacular, but it was still very good. And given its location and atmosphere, well worth eating there. Service was fine.POOL and POOL Deck: Never used it. Nothing special. Between the check in counter and TIKIs. If you must have a resort-like pool for your vacation, then don't stay here.TOURS/THINGS TO DO: There were several tourist counters in the hotel near the lobby to book activities. Very convenient. I won't comment on the individual things we did, but suffice to say, we weren't disappointed.HOTEL LOCATION: We were happy we stayed at this end of Waikiki, away from the masses. But still easy walk to everything.OVERALL: If we ever go back to Waikiki, we'll definitely stay here. No reason to take our chances elsewhere, and we were definitely pleased with our choice. Tiki's was very nice and convenient to have right at the hotel. Breakfast was a great free bargain. Not knowing anything about the other sides, I would recommend getting a view of Diamond Head (quieter, spectacular sight). And the other guests we met seemed very happy here too. We spent about $150/night for the room.

<Author>dontwantaname
<Content>Just fine We stayed at this hotel in July, 2006--and it was just fine. As others have noted, the location is great--couldn't ask for better in Waikiki. The rooms were a bit shabby (paint, carpet) but clean. We didn't have a lanai--just a 2-foot wide patio thing barely big enough to hang a swimsuit to dry. Partial ocean view means the view straight across is another building; you have to crane your neck to see the ocean. We had no problems with noise, either from the Tiki Lounge or from the ongoing renovations. Note that they no longer have access to coin laundry and the laundry service is laughably expensive ($2.95 for a pair of socks? C'mon.)The breakfast on the beach got a little monotonous after a week, but hey--it's better than paying Hawaii prices for breakfast every day. There are plenty of choices, even if they are mostly the same choices every day. The pool is small and has limited hours, but who needs a pool with a world-class beach 15 seconds away? Overall, I would recommend this hotel to families or anyone else not planning on spending much time in their room. It's not a romantic getaway spot, for sure, or a luxury hotel . But it's a reasonably priced, decent property if you want the Waikiki experience.

<Author>bethannsd
<Content>Wonderful Hotel!! I was hesitant to book at this hotel after readng some of the reviews. We booked a package through AAA and Pleasant Holidays, figuring if we were unhappy we would be able to deal with any problems through either of them. The hotel was wonderful. We have absolutely NO complaints at all. We had a wonderful semi-ocean view room, and our 2 kids (8 and 14) were in a room right next door. The rooms were brand new, very comfortable beds, nice furnishings, a flat screen tv and cable. We also had a slow but free wireless internet connection. There is a faster pay connection in each room as well as lots of inexpensive computers in the side lobby area for guests to use. The water pressure was great, the maid service was just fine, there was no noise issue at all. The AC was fine too. The free breakfast or 'breakfast on the beach' as the hotel calls it, was a total winner for us with the kids. There was fresh fruit, cereals, bagels, 4 different kinds of fresh fruit juice, numerous coffees, plus varying omelettes or quiches, or pancakes, etc each day, plus miso soup and muffins. There is live Hawaiian music and a native dancer each morning, which was so fun to listen to and watch. The 'kids eat free program' at participating restaurants was also great...but a rental car or good knowledge of the public transport system is needed to really utilize the discount fully. Cold Stone and Wolfgang Puck Express are right in the hotel...so convenient. There are always beach towels available and the beach is 50 feet away. There is a lagoon and it is perfect for kids. Larger waves are 100 feet away so there is something for everyone. The concierge staff, front desk staff, and especially Del, who works by the pool, are all so pleasant and friendly. Our stay was perfect and we would stay here again if we brought the kids. We did not eat in the hotel restauant Tiki's, but other quests said it was great. The remodel of some of the rooms that is going on was not an issue at all, there was no noise or dust. This is a perfect hotel for families. The hotel allowed us a late check out of 3 PM due to our late flight, and went out of their way to accomodate us. We would recommend this hotel to families highly. Thanks so much for a wonderful stay!

<Author>rhyannonb
<Content>Awesome! I was a bit apprehensive about staying at the ResortQuest Waikiki Beach after reading some reviews ripping the hotel apart, but decided to give them a chance anyway. I'm writing this to counter any negative reviews.The hotel has an awesome location! You can walk to many places - the beach is across the street, restaurants and stores are everywhere and the Honolulu Zoo is literally next door. The rooms were great! Yeah, they may be decorated in a Hawaiian motif you might not use in your own house, but you're in HAWAII!!! Enjoy the colorful comforters and the wood-like curtain in front of your closet space - there's nothing wrong with them. Our room was very clean and didn't appear worn or old. We had a mini fridge, tv and little balcony. We got a partial ocean view, which was just that, we could see the beach if we got close to the sliding glass door or were on the balcony. We could even see the sun set from there! Our room was on the 6th floor (which is actually 2 floors up from the lobby) and faced the pool. I got real nervous then because I remembered one reviewer complained about the noise from the pool and about the music. Uh ... I heard neither! You can hear the musician serenading the breakfast crowd if you open up your sliding door but, aside from that there was no noise that bothered us at any time of the day or night.Some reviewers complained about the monotony of the breakfast. First of all, the breakfast is FREE!!! Secondly, everyday they have cold cereal, fruit juices, muffins and sushi - aside from that, there is variation: cheese omelette one day (it's not omelette shaped and no one makes it in front of you, but it's good), sausage and egg biscuit another, tater tots, etc. They even provide you with little lunch boxes in your room to take down to breakfast, load up on goodies and go wherever you want with your FREE breakfast. The only negative: the pool is small. But then again, you can walk across the street to the vast ocean. And the area of beach across from the hotel is partially walled off so that the water right up to the wall is no more than 6 feet.Mind you, this isn't the fanciest hotel, but for the price, we got an awesome deal at a wonderful hotel! There is nothing wrong with the hotel itself, the rooms, the staff or the free breakfast. Despite the fact the hotel appears to be in good condition, the doorman advised us they're currently renovating it and should be done by the end of the year. From what he told us, they'll be installing flat screen tvs in each room and getting new the furniture and beds. I'm sure it'll be even better then, but I'm also sure someone will find fault with the renovations too. Just remember, there's just no pleasing some people. Some people expect 5 star accomodations and staff when they only paid a fraction of what it would have cost them. We were definitely more than satisfied with our 8 night stay for the price we paid.

<Content>Overall great but not for everybody I really, really want to give this hotel a better rating but due to a few issues I can't.First the good things. This hotel is in the best location in Waikiki, especially if you have small children. It is right across the street from the zoo and the park. The beach right in front has the walls which stop the waves creating a pool which is perfect for the kids. If you like waves there is plenty of them just on the other side of the concrete pier. In my opinion this is the best of both worlds. While still a very busy place we found it to be less busy than central Waikiki and still in walking distance of plenty of restaurants and shopping.The hotel itself is very nice (for waikiki) and the staff was VERY friendly. Our ocean view room was small (this seems typical for waikiki hotels) but big enough that we did not go crazy. We actually used our lanai to store things like beach toys and other outdoor items giving us a little more space in the room. The hotel offers a computer center with computers complete with webcams and internet access. There is also free wi-fi available if you bring your own computer. This was not an advretised feature and I was very surprised to see such nice ammenity.Now for the issues.This hotel has a nice pool and deck that we would loved to have used. Like many people, we were away form the hotel during the daytime hours spending time at the beach or enjoying the many sights that Oahu has to offer. On several occasions we would liked to have spent time (especially the kids) during the evening at the pool. This, however, was impossible due to the fact that the pool closes at 7:00 p.m. every evening. Very poor timing. If I wanted spend my DAYS hanging around the pool I would have just booked a hotel where I live and saved the time and money going to Hawaii. If your room is on the west side of the hotel, do not plan on going to bed early. Tikis bar and grill, located right below your room, is very active and goes past 11:00 p.m. They have live entertainment nightly and a large crowd that likes to yell a lot (mstly drunk people). To make matters worse, the seals on the sliding glass doors are poor and you get all the noise whether you like it our not.Overall,a great hotel with the best location but, unless you like to party a lot and don't mind a noisy hotel, I would use caution.

I understand it's great to be in Hawaii, but don't confuse that with an awful hotel (which this one is). <Author>GenxGem
<Content>Good location, simple accommidations First of all, I want to clarify about which hotel we stayed at. There are three hotels within 4 blocks of each other with similar names. There is the ResortQuest Waikiki Beachside, ResortQuest Waikiki Beach Tower, and ResortQuest Waikiki Beach. The first two are connected to each other, this review is for the third hotel RESORTQUEST WAIKIKI BEACH. I noticed some of the bad reviews are for the tower, which is actually a different property.The ResortQuest Waikiki Beach (formerly Aston Waikiki Beach) is a former budget hotel that's been updated with a bunch of cheezy Hawaii themed things. The rooms are nothing to speak of (there was some chipped paint and wallpaper scratched off) but it is CLEAN and the location is unbelievable. LOCATION: You are right at one end of Waikiki Beach and you can easily walk to all the shops, other hotels and tons of restaurants. The hotel is right in front of a protected part of the beach where they have put a barrier in the ocean so there are no waves (great for sm kids, I'm sure). We wanted to surf and only had to walk down a little to the part of the beach where the surfing was. The hotel is also on a corner where there is a main bus line, if you want to take public transportation.FOOD/DRINK: 1. The hotel has its' own restaurant called the Tiki Lounge. It is really great. The chef is formerly of the Palomino and it is good Hawaiian food for a good price. We're pretty big foodies and ate at Tiki's three times because our food was always so good. Go for the Mahi Mahi. Yummers. The Chocolate dessert was one of the best desserts I have ever had. It was shaped like Diamond Head. Also, if you pick up an Oahu coupon book in the lobby of the hotel, there is a coupon for a free cheesecake at Tiki's with entree purchase. 2. Breakfast on the Beach is the breakfast that is served to all guests of this hotel at no extra charge. A real plus and easy way to get everyone full before you start your day. The food is hottest when breakfast starts at 6:30am. Get there early! It's cereal, some egg dish, and something sweet along with juice, coffee, and Japanese food (fish  miso soup). Simple, but good for free. 3. There is also a Wolfgang Puck Express in this hotel. Wonderful for lunch or a quick, cheap supper. Very consistant in it's goodness. Has all the Puck staples: sandwiches, soups, salads, and pizza. 4. Starbucks is around the corner in the same building. Gotta' have the Starbucks! Cold Stone Ice Cream is also next door to Wolfgang if you need more calories.ROOM: Again, it was very clean and the maid service is amazing. The rooms themselves are pretty small, but you're not there to hang in the room. There is a lanai in each room, but only one chair, so don't plan to have a romantic dinner on your balcony. There is a safe in the room, but you have to pay $3/ day to use it. FYI.CUSTOMER SERVICE: Poor! Keith who works the front desk is horrible. When we checked in, he told us he had some availabilities for upgrades and then paused. When we thought he was going to upgrade us he said I would do it for you for $40. I said A day?! and he said yes. No way. Lame to not just upgrade us to a better room for no charge. Then, we wanted to take the bus to the Diamond Head crater and Keith gave us the wrong bus # (which wasn't operating during the holidays)and we waited for an hour with 10 other people who had followed Keith's instrtuction before splitting cabs. Finally, when we wanted to rent a car for the day, Keith told us to use the hotel's service. When we went to inquire about one, the lady told us there weren't any available and that we would need to book a tour in order to see what we wanted. We said no, walked down to the Hyatt, and rented one there. Do not use the services at this hotel, you will get a better deal at the Hyatt or book something on your own before you leave if you want to snorkel or see Pearl Harbor or something. And don't ask any questions of Keith. He won't help you.All in all, this was a good hotel for people who want to get out and do things. Don't come here on your honeymoon. It's not romantic. Do come here with families. Do come here with teenagers. Do come here as couples looking for a good price on a good location.Mahalo! Good luck with your travels.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Pleasantly Surprised I've been reading internet review sites and their precursors on usenet and BBS' for many years. Even though I should have known better, I got nervous when I read some of the extremely negative reviews for the Aston Waikiki Beach on this site. Fortunately I was pleasantly surprised by the hotel, and I hope that this will put some others' minds at ease.First, some perspective on the type of traveler I am. I stay in hotels only 2 or 3 times a year. I have no problems staying in a Motel 6 class of lodging, especially for an overnighter, but I enjoy staying in a better place if the price isn't too outrageous. I don't tend to take advantage of the amenities of a hotel beyond room perks, restaurant/bar and pool (i.e. no spa, or concierge level service for me). I'm usually travelling to enjoy something in the area, and not to spend a great deal of time in a room. I do however appreciate cleanliness, service, and a good view, and will complain if I don't feel things are up-to-snuff.Our trip to Waikiki was short - 3 nights and 4 days. We got a great rate from a travel site for the stay + airfare and it was the reason we picked this hotel over others. We did not rent a car while in town.The Aston Waikiki Beach is obviously an older building, but has been perked up by a recent renovation. The theme is best described as a kitchy take on 60's Hawaiian decor, with lots of bamboo, tikis and bright Hawaiian colors and patterns. The ground floor contains lots of shops (Wolfgang Puck's Express, the general store, Coldstone Creamery, a surfwear and accessories rental place, and perhaps a couple others) and a lounge area where you can wait for tour busses and cabs. The second floor has reception, a small pool, some computer workstations and several travel desks (including Pleasant Holidays and Expedia), as well as an area that serves the free breakfast in the morning, and dispenses towels/chairs as well as some snacks during the rest of the day. Also on the second floor is Tikis, a restaurant and bar which has very good food and friendly service.The stories people tell about the elevators do have a kernel of truth in them. We found that holding in the button for your floor, then putting your card in worked well, but as long as you press your floor while the green light is blinking you should be fine.The hallways are as people mentioned a little dim, but they spruce them up with some palm-tree projection lights at the end of the hall.Our ocean-front and ocean view rooms are pretty much exactly as pictured on the website. It is wonderful to wake up to a beautiful view of the ocean through your window, and go to bed to the moonlit water as well. The rooms aren't overly large, but not overly small either. If you want to see a small hotel room, stay on Santa Catalina Island off of Los Angeles! The bathrooms were definitely remodelled, with new tub, sink, fixtures and mirror. They did pick an odd shade of beige paint for the walls, which may make it appear a bit dingier than it really is. Nice perks in the room include a mini-fridge (empty), complimentary copies of Newsweek, and some creams and lotions beyond the usual basic soaps. Important note so you don't need to call down like we did - the hairdryer is not in the bathroom but on the top shelf of the closet. The lainai is a bit small but you can fit another chair beside the chair and ottomon already there.Breakfast is a nice affair. They have one hot breakfast-sandwich style item, cereals, fruit, muffins or cinammon rolls, some Japanese items (we saw miso soup and sushi rice cakes) and various drinks including kona coffee, milk, juice and soda. You can load it up and take it to the beach with towels and beach chairs with cupholders or eat it on the deck while a Hawaiian singer performs, usually accompanied by a dancer as well.Tikis, the in-hotel restaurant, is a great place to eat with nice wait staff and bartenders. Definitely try some of their seafood dishes for lunch or dinner.The hotel is located at the end of Waikiki beach, literally right next to a park which includes a zoo and aquarium, both worth the short time you'll need to tour through them. Directly across the street is a beach protected by a seawall. The hotel is by the deeper end, if you move toward the other end it becomes shallower until even toddlers could stand right by the seawall. The water is crystal clear and you can see schools of small fish swimming around if you take the time. A sundown swim is truly enjoyable. Beside the protected beach is another which has waves to enjoy, and stands which rent boogie boards and snorkling equipment as well.To sum up, I think this is a nice place to stay for the average traveller who is not obsessive-compulsive about every detail of their hotel. The nice perks like the free breakfast, free entertainment, free room safe and refrigerator and other small plusses in the rooms, plus good service from the staff in the hotel and restaurants, and finally its great location, should make a pleasant stay for you as long as you're paying a reasonable price.However I have to agree that the Muaka tower, which is obviously a seperate hotel, looked very run down and seedy, and I would not choose to stay there.One last tip, be sure to refer to it as the Aston Waikiki Beach around town, as almost nobody knows it by its new name.

Upon arrival, the staff was very friendly, and we received a free upgrade since we were on our honeymoon (a technicality: we never took a honeymoon 8 years ago, and have never been on a trip alone without our daughter and my daughter from a previous marriage). The room was 2312, one of the upper floors, and overlooked Diamond Head and the ocean. Why, yes, there was a view of a rooftop in front of me before the ocean, but after all, did I expect to be on a remote, barely inhabited island? At any rate, I thought the view was gorgeous and didn't mind the slim balcony - there's ample room for both of you to go out and snuggle as you take in the view!The room was very clean - more spacious than what I had envisioned from reading some of the reviews on here - there was counter space, as there was a counter extended over the toilet (not that I cared). Oh my! A wallpaper seam was visible and coming unglued and it just RUINED our entire vacation!!!! (just kidding!)There was no problem with the elevators; never took more than 1-3 minutes - what do you expect in a 25 story hotel?Breakfast was great - the only way you'd get tired of it is if you ate ALL of it every day, and how could you do that? Milk, juice, soda, bagel/omelette sandwich, yogurt, cake, muffins, fresh cut fruit, miso soup, rice, green beans? (A Japanese thing, I'm sure), almond/rice pudding, several different kinds of yogurt...how can you COMPLAIN about FREE sustenance??? No, it wasn't dining at the Ritz-Carleton, but neither was I paying for it either!!!Go to Pearl Harbor the first day, as you will be up at the crack of dawn - we took the bus for $2, but I would recommend one of the services that have been recommended on here for $8 round-trip -- it took us over an hour on the city bus. We then took the trolley out front (pink line) to the Ala Moana Mall for $2.Dinner at Tiki's was good and not terribly expensive -and so convenient!Day 2: Hiked Diamond Head and did the Polynesian Cultural Center - wish we had gone at 10 a.m. on the bus rather than 12...get Cousin Ken as a tour guide if you can - he's awesome!Day 3  4 - rented a car, snorkeled at Hanauma bay (poor visibility), drove around Honolulu - day 4, drove around the island...Day 5: Walked around Waikiki Beach prior to departure.You MUST go to Duke's and have a drink...or two...Souvenirs are good at Walmart - I bought 10k turtle earrings for $65 made in Hawaii - most souvenirs you'll find are made in China or Philippines.Oahu Revealed is a MUST BUY! Gives you GREAT information.Snorkeling at Shark's Cove was incredible - you MUST rent a car for a couple of days and drive around the island; I recommend doing it after the PCC so you will have a better sense of the lay of the land - and we even saw a sea turtle on Turtle Beach! We stopped at a roadside fruit stand and got an ice-cold coconut to drink - can't beat it!Our trip was the best ever - and I tend to be disappointed after building trips up in my head prior to arrival - but the hotel or Hawaii did not let me down.I would compare the quality of the hotel to a Fairfield Inn or Hampton Inn. If you want luxury, please pay for it and don't gripe - my husband didn't want to stay at a luxury hotel b/c he finds them stuffy. By the way, I have a barely used Entertainment book for Hawaii for sale for $10, a $35 retail value - email me for more details! The day before we left, a woman with a tour group was griping about her room - that she had a view of a ROOF - and I asked her if she paid for an oceanview room, to which she sputtered...No....bottom line, if you want a great view, you have to pay for the oceanfront or oceanview room. We had booked a partial ocean view and were upgraded to ocean view. But don't expect a totally unobstructed view - book oceanfront. God bless and mahalo!

In fact, we walked to McDonalds on our final morning. We had a partial ocean-view room and the view was alright, but the balcony was very small. For example, a chair could not fit on it. The best part about this hotel is that it is located in a great location. With just a little bit of walking, you can get to shops, restaurants, the beach, the zoo, and the International Marketplace. For most of the attractions, such as the dinner cruises, submarines, and luaus, a shuttle picks up right outside the hotel. The valet parking was pretty good and seemed to be pretty fast; just don鈥檛 forget anything in your car or you鈥檒l have to wait for them to pull your car around just to get the item out. The internet kiosks are very reasonable and have fast connections.In conclusion, I would probably not stay at this place again unless I got a dirt cheap rate. We both wished that we had chosen another property like the Hilton Hawaiian village or the Hyatt Regency instead. This hotel did not meet our expectations but it certainly did not ruin our trip. This hotel is in a great location and is clean and comfortable, but I would rate it at 1.5 stars because it seems cheap.

<Content>Everything I Had Hoped We just returned from staying a week in the main hotel tower at the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel, and all of us (me, my husband, and two teenage daughters) thoroughly enjoyed our stay. Our problem was sharing one bathroom with two teenage girls, but I can't blame that on the hotel! We had a beautiful view of Diamond Head and the beach. In fact, I could often look out onto the beach and see our daughters. The elevators were fine; they are not slow. Any perceived slowness is due to the fact that they're constantly in use by the hotel guests, and even then we never waited long. The location of this hotel is terrific! The beach is right across the street and, though still quite busy and hopping with people, you're a couple of blocks away from where it starts getting really congested with people out dining and shopping. Some shopping and dining on the premises, with better and many more choices nearby. All four of us loved the breakfast--there was something for everyone, and we never had to buy lunch. All in all, we had a great experience and stay at this hotel and will definitely return in the future. It's not the Sheraton, but then....we didn't pay to stay at the Sheraton!

For the most part they were loud; rude; obnoxious; ill-mannered; miss-behaved and out of control. They would crowd in to the elevators before the folks in the elevator could get out. They would run up and down the halls shouting and screaming. They would cut in line. Another housekeeper was sparyed with something (maybe hair spray) and was blinded for a period of time. These kids broke matresses and trashed rooms. Unless you are into this, maybe you should find another hotel. We won,t stay there again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Positive Overall Experience Based on some of the stories we read about some 3 star hotels in Honolulu not being what they were cracked up to be we were a bit apprehensive about the Aston Waikiki Beach. As it turned out the property was just fine. The location is in fact excellent (right across from the beach area) and the room was quite acceptable. Relatively clean. Amazing quiet given the fact that our room was right next to the elevator. And get this . We never waited more than 3-5 minutes for an elevator in either direction at any time day or night. Go figure.... We could see Diamond Head from our 21st floor lanai and could catch a slice of the beach if you looked hard right. But guess what...you shouldn't have to rely on your room to get a view of the ocean. Get your buns out and see the world up close and personal! It's much more fun. The real bonus is the free breakfast. Decent grub, live music, serve yourself, and take as much as you want. We were there for three days and never had lunch since we filled up at breakfast and took along a load of snacks snacks for the road. My wife is Japanese American and was pleasantly surprised with the vast array of Japanese style breakfast fare available. Miso soup, rice, somen noodles, etc. Plus as great array of standard breakfast grub. Be sure to try the mini muffins. They'll go over pretty well on the power drive up to the North Shore or out to the Polynesian Cultural Center. Our two year old loved the individual servings of Cheerios and Fruit Loops that he could haul around.The staff was outstanding from the valets, to the front desk, to housekeeping. They treated us like we were the only guests there in spite of the crowds.Don't get me wrong this is not the Ritz (we stayed there on Maui after leaving the Aston), but for the dough this venue packs a really great value.Clean, safe, relatively quite where it needs to be quiet and hoppin' where should be. Close to the action and a known quantity via the Aston namesake. We would go back in a heartbeat. We stayed March 7-10, 2005 and paid $138/night via (---).

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice location, friendly service We just got back from Waikiki February 2, 2005 and stayed at the Aston for 10 days. We read the reviews before leaving and were not disappointed with the hotel. We had gotten a pretty good deal with Expedia when we booked the hotel. Upon arriving in Honolulu the ground transportation area was confusing and the phones to call for shuttles didn't work, we ended up just getting in a taxi ($24 to the hotel). Upon return to airport make a reservation with one of the shuttles ($5 one way). When we arrived,the check-in was quick and friendly. Brian got us into a room with a nice view, pool side facing the ocean. Shortly after getting into the room he had a small bottle of champagne delivered with two fluted glasses. The rooms are not very big but certainly large enough to get around. The location is very nice for going to the beach (right across the street). You could return back to the room from the beach with little effort for drinks, etc. We enjoyed the BOB each morning. We never took the breakfast to the beach but there was always room around the pool area to sit and read the paper (free on your door each morning). The staff are all very friendly, we left $5 for our maid (Nora) every few days and she was wonderful. She even gave me a hug towards the end of the week out of appreciation for the small tip. Our only problem we experienced while there was one afternoon we returned to our room and found the the door was locked from the inside. When it was opened we found a maid that was not our normal person. We called the supervisor of house keeping and complained. House Keeping spoke to the maid who said she was adding soaps etc. It still didn't explain why she locked the door. The supervisor apologized, sent us a nice card along with an very nice hard cover book about Hawiaii as a gift. We didn't see the maid the rest of our stay. I would recommend using a safe anytime one is available at a hotel. My wife and I are both in law enforcement and see several thefts from local hotels that are suspected to be committed by staff. Many hire temp., seasonal, and part-time help without any backgrounds being done. Over-all we would go back to the Aston if there again. You are close to everything that Waikiki is know for.

<Content>not disappointed at all I had booked the Aston at the last minute as we just decided to go within a few days(first week of feb 2005). They had french toast sticks, egg and meat on a bagel/bun, muffins, milk, cereal, bagels and cream cheese, pastry and some asian dishes. All the fruit you wanted and tea, coffee and juices. It was great and saved us at least 25-30 a day for 4 of us. Last time in Hawaii I had a hotel room that had bugs, I must say in the 8 days we stayed here we never seen one bug in our hotel room. The hotel is located right across the street from the beach, like 30 seconds and you are there. It is down the quieter end of Waikiki and close to everything, walking distance to the zoo and aquarium.Less than 10 minutes. I was eating breakfast one morning when I overheard a traveller talking to the manager and he was complimenting her on how well kept the hotel was. It was clean and the atmosphere was very welcoming. every morning they had a singer as well as a hula dancer. They also had entertainment at night as well. The safe they have in the room is worth it and a good size. Most I have seen only fit wallets and small cameras. this one fit a laptop,cameras, wallets etc.Well worth the $2.00 a day. As far as security for the hotel, you cannot get to any of the floors unless you have a key. You have to stick your key in first and then select your floor.I would have no problem recommending this hotel.

<Content>Not worth it The best part about this hotel is the location. It is right across from the beach -- you just walk across the street and then you're there. We were in Hawaii for two weeks the last time we visited, and planned to stay the whole time at this hotel. The Islander, though not as kitschy, as least allowed us to sleep through the night. Don't be fooled into buying a room in the Mauka Tower -- we made this mistake the first time we stayed here and were dismayed to find ourselves in the smaller shack out behind the new hotel, in a room which reeked of smoke, where the air conditioner was broken, and we could not open the door to the lanai. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Everything in Perspective - It's not Bad at all. We just returned from a 6 night stay at the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel and I must say we had a great time. The staff we encountered, Del at the Valet was nothing but pleasant and Helpful EACH and every time we saw him. Keith at the front desk was helpful as well when Expedia messed up our reservation and the reservation information was not there - thank goodness we packed a copy of our itinerary. Everyone at the Hotel staff, Breakfast setup, TIKI's Bar, Valet, Maid Service was Friendly and Helpful. As for the rooms, OK so they are small. But we were not paying $400 or $500 a night so we did not expect the Kahala Mandarin Oriental Hilton. We had an OCEAN FRONT room on the 12th floor and did not encounter any of the problems listed in other reviews. Our view was spectacular - the sunset was right on the money. If we leaned over the balcony just a bit we could see the edge of Diamond Head. Each night we could see the lighting of the beach torches. We did not hear the bar noise (although it was 7 floors or so directly below us on ocean front) - Our room was clean (and cleaned EACH DAY) - sure the carpet was a little worn and the bathroom could have used a remodel job but the water pressure was strong. The dresser space was LIMITED. So we utilized the shelf space in the closet with the BEADED curtain which was cute. As for the decor - hey it's Hawaii - it's supposed to be big flower prints! The elevators (or lifts) if you please were right on the money so I am not sure what the fuss about them being slow is all about. We never had to wait more than a minute.The LOCATION can't be beat. It's directly across the street from the beach, towels and folding sling chairs are provided free of charge. There is not a lot of street/people traffic in front of the hotel like the other hotels on the main drag. There is a Starbucks, Cold Stone Creamery and Wolfgang Puck within a handful of steps. On Sunday Night they host a movie on the beach and we could see the screen from our balcony but opted for a closer view and headed to the beach where everyone was congregating watching Spiderman 2 and eating Ice cream etc. Due to the excellent location, we did not rent a car, most things were walking distance or trolley away. The BREAKFAST, while basic, is more than acceptable, yogurt (3 varieties each day), mini muffins (3-4 varieties), Coffee cake, cold cereal, hot egg mcmuffin type sandwiches, Miso Soup, Spinach Quiche, fresh fruit cups, coconut jello and a full beverage bar (milk, coffee, Guava, Pineapple, Orange, Lemonade and Sodas) are available. There is no limit/maximum on what you can take so fill your bags and make a second trip as our room had a REFRIGERATOR so we took some sodas and yogurts for later in the day.TIKI's Bar is great - the drinks are plentiful, the views of the sunset are spectacular. As For FOOD- we HIGHLY recommend Sensei Japanese Steak House at the neighboring Marriott. It was EXCELLENT. LULU's is also next door - more of a bar/restaurant atmosphere but fun and upbeat. LUAU, we did the Paradise Cove (the all inclusive $100 per person package) and while the show was nice and the beach location lovely, the food was substandard (fried Chicken, Macaroni Salad and the PIG) the drinks (7each with the package we purchased) we small but you could supersize them for an additional $3. It got a little chilly as the night wore on - something they don't tell you - but Paradise Cove makes out like bandits sellling sweatshirts and lightweight jackets for $29 and up. We had a late flight so we asked for a later checkout but the hotel was full due to the golf event but we were offered a room in the Mauka tower for $60 with a 6pm checkout. It was ONLY when we went to the Mauka Tower that we understood the negative reviews. The Mauka Tower reminded us of those early 1980's rentals in Wildwood NJ where Teenagers grouped together in rooms because it was a cheap way to enjoy the beach. This tower is not pretty and while part of the hotel should not be used as the focal point to judge the hotel. If your budget means you can only afford the Mauka Tower room, then avoid this hotel. Instead pick a hotel that is a street or two from the beach, like the Radisson, but realize that the Radisson (or any other 2 street in hotel is not going to be ocean view but rather Hotel/apartment building view)Now I am sure after this rather lengthy review, you are as skeptical as I was when readling all of the reviews. On what travel experience is the reviewer's opinion based? Well we have traveled extensively and stayed at some of the top rated hotels in the World: The Hotel de Paris in Monte Carlo, The Kahala Mandarin Oriental in Hawaii on our last stay in Hawaii), The Hotel George V in Paris, El San Juan Hotel in Puerto Rico, Le Chateau Frontenac in Quebec, Bora Bora Lagoon in French Polynesian islands. So what made us choose the Aston Waikiki Beach? We wanted a quick longer than a weekend getaway which was affordable and had a desirable location. In our case, we preferred to spend our money on good food , drinks and other activities - spending time in the room was not a main priority. As long as it was neat, clean and had a great view......Feel free to contact us.

The safe box in our room was nice to have and we did not have to pay for it when we departed (at least nothing was said and no expense incurred). The location is wonderful because you're still on, and in, the Waikiki strip but on the end and a bit removed from the main central strip of Waikiki and still within a nice walking distance. In short, for those of you who are thinking of staying there for your trip to Honolulu, it is definitely a great place and great location. There was absolutely nothing wrong with this hotel. It was fun and a nice experience. Aloha!

<Content>Great Value...fun place! We stayed at the Aston Wakiki Beach Hotel for 2 nights, last week and really enjoyed ourselves. The food at Tiki's was really good and the atmosphere fun. For $120-150 a night, you could do much worse and not have nearly the view or location at Waikiki.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Experience My husband and I just returned from spending 6 nights at the Aston Waikiki Beach hotel on the 26th and I am amazed at all the totally different perceptions of it. We had an oceanview room on the 19th floor with a King sized bed that was quite comfortable. The room was small, but clean and the refrigerator and insulated cooler were nice for drinks and snacks. The maid service was very prompt, the front desk was friendly and helpful and left us a complimentary bottle of champagne as we were celebrating our anniversary. The breakfast isn't gourmet food, but a definite step above a continental breakfast that was great to grab something to eat before heading off to see or do something that we went to hawaii for. We loved having a cup of coffee on our balcony first thing in the morning and a drink there before going out at night. We paid around $135 a night with a package deal and while there are some really beautiful hotels on Waikiki, feel that for the money and opportunity to go to Hawaii the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel is absolutely fine and would stay there again.

And the bathtub/shower was very VERY slow draining- (a bit of background- there were 4 of us 20-something year old girls staying in the room so showering after the beach was NOT a fun experience as you were standing in about 5 inches of some one elses dirty sandy water!). All in all though, this is a great hotel, and very good for the price! I would definately stay here again and recommend it to anyone travelling to Hawaii. On my previous trip to Honolulu, I stayed at the Outrigger East (now called the Ohana East) which definately was not up to the standard of this hotel. I hope this review was helpful!

<Content>Not a resort but a great place to start If you've been to the islands of Hawaii you know there are distinct differences between them all with Oahu being one of the busiest  most populated, with that in mind the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel is a great value for the area. In my case it's two teenaged girls but if it was two 6' boys definately too small.Pros: Less crowded location (by Waikiki standards). <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A 2 star hotel at 4 star prices This was our fourth trip to Hawaii and we had stayed in Aston hotels 3 out of those 4 times. This Aston property was a major disappointment. It is old, the one elevator was tiny, the rooms were small, furnishings smelled old and musty, we tried but could not upgrade our room to the full ocean view. Others in our group did MUCH better at the Sheraton Waikiki and Outriggers on the beach for less money. Aston should remove its name from this hotel or tear it down and build a new one in its place. What we learned from this trip was (a) do not take a prepaid all-inclusive package from a web site that will not allow us to change hotels without losing most of the money, (b) be cautious when a hotel is described as charming, or boutique by a travel site, (c) have a healthy respect for TripAdvisor reviews, several of which reflected my own eventual experience at this hotel, (c) definitely not come back to this hotel. There are far better deals on the beach.

<Author>momwith4boys
<Content>2nd stay and loved it again!! This was our 2nd stay there this year; the first was over New Year and the second was for a week July 7-16. We stayed in both the ocean view and ocean front rooms and the views were just breathtaking. In both instances, the views also have some of the Honolulu skyline so that at night, you can see the beautiful lights when you can't really see the ocean. It was very convenient to cross the street and go to the beach with the towels and chairs they provide. Tiki's restaurant is absolutely gourmet and we ate there so many times trying all the different dishes. Wolfgang Puck Express is downstairs and also very reasonable. Both these are available on the room service menu which makes it about the best room service menu I've seen. We've travelled a lot to resorts in the Caribbean and Mexico, and this is still one of our favorites (we'd like it better if it were all inclusive since we have 4 kids). The breakfast doesn't taste that great, especially the hot items, but usually everyone could find something to fill themselves up (cereal, pastries, fruit, yogurt) so it saved us a lot of money -- the coffee was strong and good. And we could take some things back to the room and put them in the fridge for later which was also a plus. All the employees were very pleasant, especially the valet guys who gave us good ideas on local places to eat. The beach directly across is protected so very safe for little ones, but just a block down the Kapiolani park beach has waves for those who like to boogie board. Also, they show movies on a giant screen every weekend on the beach and lots of people went to watch (we could see it from our room). Ask for a high floor for a better view. For a great and different selection of inexpensive food go to the food court in the Ala Moana shopping center. Our favorite was Yummy's, a Korean chain where we ate Kalbi, the Korean crosscut ribs. Overall, we'd go back to the Aston Waikiki beach hotel again because of the convenient location, awesome views, and Tikis!!!! Feel free to email me with any more questions.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location We stayed at the Aston from June 27-July 3 and found it to be a good deal and a great location. I found the breakfast on the beach to be fun and very accomodating--good food choices and plenty to eat. The hotel has beach towels and beach chairs that you can check out daily. The Aston is one of the few hotels on Waikiki Beach without an interrupted view of the ocean. There is no property in front of the hotel so you can easily view the sea. We were upgraded for no additional cost to a full oceanview room, which was well worth it. The views are stunning. I liked the little balconies. I spent my mornings with the newspaper, watching the waves roll in. It was quite peaceful. The hotel restaurants are good--Wolfgang Puck Express, Cold Stone and Tikis Bar and Grill. Tikis has live music and has a spirited environment. Also, several free trolleys and cheap trolleys ($2 per person) make their stops at the Aston. There is an Expedia person in the hotel lobby to help you book your day trips. I didn't pay for a five star hotel, so I didn't expect to stay in one. However, I was very pleased with the service, the pool, the environs and the aloha spirit. I would stay here again.
