<Author>Keystone_Cruiser
<Content>Enjoyed our stay at the Aston and the great views We stayed at the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel from July 2-5. It was a very pleasant stay. I will agree that the elevators are the number 1 area that needs improvement. They are extremely slow and there are not enough of them for the size of hotel it is. We had two balcony rooms on the sixth floor overlooking the pool area. They were very nice as they afforded us wonderful views of Waikiki, downtown Honolulu and the sunset over the western Ohau mountains. Since it was July 4th on Sunday of our stay, we got to see fireworks! From our balcony, we were treated to both the Pearl Harbor fireworks display in the distance and then the Ala Moana Shopping Center display closer to us. Very nice! The only problem with these rooms are that they are right above the bar area and they have live performances until midnight. The music though was actually soothing and helped put us to sleep since it was not rock, but Hawaiian. The newly renovated pool area is wonderful and the fact that you are right across the street from Waikiki beach is nice also. An added plus is that you can sign beach towels and beach chairs out for your use on the beach. I found the desk clerks to be helpful. I have to agree that room cleaning times leave something to be desired. We went on a tour at 6:30 a.m. and returned at 1:00 p.m. to find that our room had not yet been cleaned. She then came about an hour later and we had to vacate the room so that she could clean. The restaurant, Tiki's, is very nice and reasonably priced for Waikiki. There are some nice shops on the ground level and the hotel location lends itself to great additional shopping in the area. It is also close to the Honolulu Zoo, Diamond Head and the park. The Waikiki Movies on the Beach take place on the beach right across from the hotel and the shuttle to the Ala Moana Shopping Mall has a pick-up station right in front of the hotel. The hotel, like many in Waikiki, is older and the hall and room carpets are worn, but they do the best they can. The floor looked swept and the bathroom was clean and we got fresh towels each day. The large balconies are wonderful. The only other negative that I want to point out is the bus pick-up area. Many tour busses and trolley's use the street just to the west of the hotel for pick-ups and drop offs. This can create quite a back-up on the street. It also creates havoc as you try to find your bus amongst a sea of similar looking vehicles. Perhaps a bus attendent could be stationed out there to either direct bus traffic OR at least keep track of what busses are out there to help direct people. There are also about a half dozen parking spaces on the street next to the hotel, perhaps those could be eliminated and that area used for additional bus or trolley stopping/loading areas. We stayed at the Radisson Prince Kuhio the last time we were in Waikiki and enjoyed it too, but the Aston Waikiki Beach is now our first choice if we go back!

They have Movies on the Beach on Friday, Saturday and Sunday nights, right across the street. There is a nice boardwalk and sitting area across the street and there is a reef to snorkel in and a surfing area in the water directly across the street. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>My Honest Opinion of the AWBH Most of the average/below average reviews are accurate on this hotel. I will hold nothing back in my review. The PROS about the Aston Wakiki Beach Hotel (AWBH):It is in a great location at the end of the Waikiki beach strip, so overcrowding was not a problem. You can come and go to the beach as you please with no hassle. It is located atop a Starbucks, Wolfgang Pucks, and Cold Stone Creamery...definitely a plus. If you don't want to pay $13 a day for hotel parking, you can park at the zoo which is only half a block away from the hotel. There is metered parking for 25 cents an hour. The all-you-can-eat breakfast bar helped us save money on breakfast. Every morning they have fresh fruit, coffee, juice, as well as a variety of other foods such as soba noodle salad, miso soup, and sausage biscuits. We stocked up on fresh fruit, cereal, and cinnamin rolls every day. Tiki's Bar  Grill is located by the pool and it has a very festive atmosphere. Every day after 3pm there is a good live band that plays oldies and other popular songs. When you are lying on the beach and relaxing, you can hear the band several yards away and it is very refreshing. The staff was courteous and helpful.Now, the CONS about the AWBH:We stayed in the renovated section of the hotel with a partial ocean-view. The hotel room is average, if not below average. It is large enough to accomodate two full-size beds and a bureau. There is almost no balcony space on the side we were at. It wasn't even large enough to place a single chair out there to sit and relax. Instead of a regular closet door to store your bags, they use a cheap  tacky beaded curtain. The ironing board had stains on it. The mini-fridge looked about 15 years old and wasn't even stocked. The lobbies smelled of smoke and it doesn't take a professional eye to see that the carpet and wall decor was not part of the 30 million dollar renovation. The most disappointing part of the hotel room was the bathroom. It was clearly not part of the renovation as the walls were kept in their oiriginal beige paint color. You get fresh towels and some cheap shampoo every day. But no cup to rinse, no shower cap, no shower gel. The bathroom was so small and cramped that if one person takes a shower, they can't help but get the WHOLE bathroom wet and damp. Nothing luxurious about that. We are not picky people, but the hotel room had nothing to offer except a clean bed every night. It propelled us to spend very little time than necessary in our room. When I wanted to take naps, I opted to take them on the beach to avoid the dinginess of our hotel room. I will not stay here again, because I know there are better hotels to stay at. I realized that spending a couple hundred extra dollars makes a big difference in quality. Even though the hotel supposedly spent 30 million dollars in renovations, you can tell that they cut corners and cheated us out of quality and comfort.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Location!!!! My husband and I stayed from May 14-19, 2004 at this hotel and it was great! This hotel had more than we expected. The Wolfgang Puck's and Coldstone's were right underneath the hotel. We visited those locations multiple times. The beach is right across the street and they offer weekend events on that section of the beach. No need to walk a couple of blocks, it's right there! For those of you needing your Starbucks, there is a Starbucks located on the same block as the hotel. Just keep walking past Coldstone's and the ABC store and it's right there on the corner. Just a block or two up the street is the Waikiki Aquarium. Great place to visit if you like sea animals and it's cheap. If you are a student from any college or high school, make sure you bring your school ID. It's only 5 bucks to get in. We had read in another tripadvisor comment, that the elevators took forever, well, on our trip they were fast and prompt. There are five elevators to take you to your floor. We didn't eat at Tiki's because there was a LONG wait to get in. I would suggest that you make reservations ahead since that is a happening place at night. The breakfast buffet was great but my husband didn't like the warm breakfast (hashbrowns too greasy and the egg biscuit/bagel/muffin[it changes daily] felt like he was eating foam eggs). The fresh fruit and cold cereal was perfect (If you drink skim milk, you are out of luck, they only have 2% milk) as well as the bakery goods. If you like miso soup, that's also available too. The best part of the breakfast was having the opportunity to walk across the street and sit on the sand or beach table to eat your breakfast. The last morning we were there, the pool finally OPENED. The view from the pool to the beach is awesome. Don't miss an opportunity to eat breakfast poolside. The service was excellent and the rooms were clean. We were on the 24th floor and our room had a front door view of Diamondhead and our window had a partial ocean view. Decent sized room and the bed was comfy too. I would definately recommend this hotel and would stay there again. Aloha!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>excellent location and innovative attitude I stayed at the Aston Waikiki Beach hotel in late March 2004, after extensive research of area hotels. My goal was to find a reasonably priced, beach-adjacent or beachfront hotel on the quieter, greener Diamond Head side of Waikiki. Not only did the Aston fulfill these requirements of good location and value (my room was less than $150/night), but it also renewed my interest in this particular chain, which has innovatively pointed the way for other Waikiki hotels. For starters, the colorful, slightly kitschy rooms reflect a fun, young sensibility that鈥檚 a welcome alternative to the boxy, beiged-out rooms in every other local mid-priced hotel. Moreover, the informal Tiki鈥檚 restaurant is affordably priced, offering a good selection of casual food and drinks, with live music around the clock (which might be a problem if you don鈥檛 like the music). While the pool is relatively small, the hotel is next to the best beaches in Waikiki, and there鈥檚 always some weekend fair at adjacent Kapiolani park. General Manager Mark DeMello is accessible and responsive, and allayed my concerns about smoky-smelling rooms (complaints I鈥檇 read about online), making sure my registration process went smoothly. Of course, the signature feature of this hotel well may be its 鈥渂reakfast-on-the-beach鈥?program, for which guests fill up collapsible containers with various breakfast items arranged in a buffet at poolside. It鈥檚 not gourmet food, but it鈥檚 tasty, filling, and allows one to eat on the go. It鈥檚 hard to believe that other hotels haven鈥檛 already copied this idea. Overall, this hotel has the right combination of fun, casual style, excellent location, and exceptional value; I definitely plan to stay here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good for Families The location of this property made up for its shortcomings. A short walk to wonderful Kapiolani Park (neat little zoo) and right across the street from a quiet section of the beach, we were happy to be removed a bit from the crowds, yet close enough to walk up to the action. It's definitely an urban environment, which was an interesting change from the outer islands we usually visit. That said, the older Makua Tower looked pretty seedy and I would avoid it.The main part of the hotel was fine, nothing fancy, 2-3 stars, which was all we expected. We found the new decor cute, and our little girls (3  6) loved the green surfboards in the open air lobby . Our ocean view room had a K bed and a fold-out couch for the kids. The view was 90degrees of beach/ocean and 90degrees Marriott across the street, but we did have two balconies with chairs and small tables. Clearly much of the remodel $$ went toward non-sexy costs such as safety retrofits. (Which I appreciated as I watched a toddler across the way fitting his head between the balcony rails a the Marriott.) It's too bad that more couldn't have been spent on the Aston's small grungy bathrooms, that's really my biggest complaint. All the staff we encountered were friendly and helpful. The breakfast was very convienent as it allowed us to have our usual cereal and start the day without the hassle of a sit-down restaurant, but the hot foods weren't very appealing. So know going in, your money is getting you a moderate hotel with a tiny pool and a great location. It's downtown and it's noisy. This is not a peaceful paradise retreat, but a great base of operations for a busy family on the go.

I checked my kids out out and into the Waikikii Banyon where they enjoyed a spectacular condo at exactly one-half the price. Buyer beware!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Pleasantly Surprised I must say I was pleasantly surprised. I stayed at the hotel Jan 19 to the 23, 2004. Since this was my first trip to Oahu and my first trip with my mom, I wanted to ensure we had clean, comfortable accommodations close to the beach so I took the time to research hotels and decided to book w/Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel. I booked a few weeks in advance. I was a little apprehensive and almost cancelled my reservations after reading the reviews a few days before departing to Oahu. Thankfully I did not cancel. As my mother is considered a senior, we were automatically upgraded (no charge) from a partial ocean view to an almost full ocean view. We were on the 20th floor and had an amazing view. Had it not been for the view, I know the trip would have been far less enjoyable. The room itself was fairly basic. Two twin beds, a TV, refrigerator, full bath, hair dryer, iron c/w ironing board. Everything was clean and working as it should be.The hotel itself has a heated pool which I used. Went to Tiki s Bar and Grill. The food was okay and so were the prices. There is a live band that plays til about midnight. I could hear them loud and clear from the 20th floor. I don t believe there was much of anything else worth checking out. The fact this is rated as a 4 star hotel hhhmmm . It doesn t have that much to offer. I found it odd the lounge (if you can call it that) or the seating area is an open area across from the street and parking lot entrance exit.The three things that made this hotel worth staying at: one) the location of the hotel; two) the view from the 20th floor (note: try asking for odd room #s 2015 to 2021, not sure which tower, however if you are facing the reception desk, it s the tower to the right ); three) the breakfast (if you eat enough or pack enough you are set for lunch).The service was good and guests were friendly.Overall I would give it a 3-1/2 stars out of five. Personally, I don't think you can go wrong with the hotel itself as long as you are in a clean room with a spectacular view.

<Author>phisig21
<Content>Great location -- so,so overall This hotel definitely has a lot of mixed reviews. We stayed 12.27.03-1.3.04. Below are my specific comments. My overall rating at the end.Breakfast -- FAIR. Good hours (who really wants to sleep in while in Hawaii? Sleep at home!), food is a typical buffet style -- good if you like the exotic offerings like Japanese style foods, avoid the scary egg sandwiches, not enough fresh fruit/juice choices.Rooms -- OK. Not too large (common in Hawaii) but livable. In room mini fridge and big shower a nice touch. We requested non-smoking, but got smoking (I think from the ashtray in the room) but the room was not smelly or anything. Maid service was GREAT! Room always made up well, clean sheets/towels/extras when you ask. Just make sure to put the not now sign on when you go to bed each night and change to service when you leave for the morning ... otherwise you will get a greeting around 7 AM! The view (we had ocean view) was true to the photo on expedia. Very nice. Only real complaint was the amount of noise from the side street in back of the hotel -- garbage pickup daily at about 6 AM. The walls could stand to be a little thicker.Hotel amenities -- FAIR. Hotel restaurants are good and Tiki's offers a limited room service menu. Great drinks at reasonable prices! Expedia travel desk almost makes up for the fact there is no concierge...almost. The front desk, while busy was usually helpful -- the men are definitely friendlier than the women for some reason. Pool? Small and REALLY cold, but OK. They really need a hot tub - they totally have room for it. DON'T use the phone in the room. They charge 75 cents for local and 800 calls ... even when you get a busy signal and they don't connect. I used to work in management for a Marriott property and I can tell you this is NOT standard practice!Location -- EXCELLENT! I really don't think for the money you can do better. The beach directly across the street is part of Waikiki Beach, yet is is less crowded and more park-like, yet still has rentals and lifeguards. Nice trees for shade too! Only a short walk to the busier beach sections and larger hotels.OVERALL -- This is NOT a 4-star/4-palms hotel as advertised. This hotel is equivalent to a nicer Holiday Inn property. I think that people who go believing the advertisements will be disappointed. You have to remember that any hotel, in any location will only point out the good not the bad. I would stay here again is traveling to Oahu if I wanted to stay in the same budget for hotel -- paying more I will definitely stay at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider -- awesome place!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not too bad, but not all that great My husband, kids (ages 3 and 9 months), parents and sister stayed at the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel Dec. 26 thru Jan 2. We had been anticipating this vacation since early summer. After reading some of the horror stories about this hotel, I contacted the hotel with my concerns. They were very friendly and offered to upgrade our rooms for free. I was very impressed with their prompt responses and their courtesy. Our vacation, however, turned out to be a bit disappointing. Since we requested two adjoining rooms, we got the adjoining rooms but we didn't get our free upgrade after all. Our partial ocean view rooms had tiny lanais without any furniture (like expedia advertised) and a very partial view of the ocean. The rooms were ok, small, but mostly clean. Pretty much what I expected from the internet pictures. The free breakfast was good, but they offered basically the same things every day. I was hoping there would be some kind of variation. Parking was pretty bad most of the time, but the valets were very friendly and worked really hard! (From our experience, the hotel staff was very courteous and friendly.) The elevators were crowded most of the time, too. Overall, I was happy with our stay but we probably won't stay there again. I have to admit, however, that the disappointments of our vacation were not necessarily hotel-related. Christmas-time is one of the craziest times of year in Waikiki. Everywhere was crowded. We spent most of our time waiting in lines. Also, the weather was awful. It rained 6 out of our 8 days there. My daughter came down with strep throat the first day we got there. So, I don't blame it all on the Aston. My best advice is don't stay there if you're really picky about your hotels, and don't go to Waikiki during peak season.

<Author>joel90069
<Content>Lower Your Expectations The problem with the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel is the way everyone seems to insist on promoting it. It's not a bad place but after reading some of the travel websites (particularly Expedia) your expectations are higher then they should be. Still, for the cost it was a reasonable value. The rooms are a step up from a high rise Motel 6. After upgrading I had a beautiful view but the furniture and bathrooms seemed old and seedy. Most of the employees I came in contact with were quite nice, helpful and customer service oriented. They just didn't have much to work with. The location was terrific but Waikiki itself leaves a lot to be desired. I felt like I was in Los Angeles with coconut trees. Use the hotel as a base of operation. Rent a car and explore the rest of the island everyday. I found several beaches that were beautiful, isolated and secluded.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Enjoyed our Stay at the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel I was worried about this hotel after reading some of the previous reviews about what a terrible hotel this was. I worried needlessly!! I truly enjoyed my stay at the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel. It is close to everything yet not right in the middle of the hustle and bustle of Waikiki. I reserved an ocean front room and it had a fantastic view (Waikiki at night is beautiful). The room wasn't large, but it was clean. The ocean front rooms are decorated in red and white with dark teak furniture. The breakfast on the beach has a large selection of food (cereal, egg sandwiches, yogurt, miso soup, noodles, hash browns, fruit, muffins, bagels, almond and coconut gelatin, milk, coffee, juice, tea). Anything that we had left over was put into the refrigerator for a snack later. Tiki's is a great place for lunch or dinner. The food is great and price are reasonable (the ribs with guava sauce are great). Also try the Coldstone Creamery in the front of the hotel..excellent ice cream and you get to pick what you want to add(cookies, nuts, chips, coconut,...). As many reviewers have pointed out, the valet parking is a bit expensive at $12.50 per day. However, it is great to pull up at the hotel entrance, have someone help with packages, and not have to worry about finding a parking space. It usually didn't take more than 5 minutes for the car to be delivered in the morning. Everyone was extremely helpful with directions, places to go, and things to do. The hotel kept our luggage for us until we were ready to leave for the airport (6:00 pm) at no charge. I would definitely stay at the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel again.

After doing a lot of research for a weeklong trip that I won from King's Hawaiian Bread, I chose this hotel for my 4yo daughter, 68yo mother, and 44yo me. My mother was a bit skeptical about the mixed reviews, but we wanted something CLOSE to the beach, with restaurant alternatives near by, different from every cookie-cutter hotel, and NOT in the middle of town. The Aston Hawaiian Beach Hotel fit the bill!Breakfast was a great bonus and the extra yogurts and cereal rounded out a lunch or two (the refrigerator in the room was another great amenity). The free beach chairs were great; we used them when watching the Aloha parade on the street right in front of the hotel!We upgraded to a Jr Suite, 15th floor, that seemed to be the one from the webcam on the hotel's website...great views of the sunset, the surfers, and Waikiki from the lanai(s). Tiki's often had music that we enjoyed in the late afternoon and into the night (ended at 10 or 11 every night). We could hear it, but it was not loud enough to keep us awake (we didn't turn on the tv) and we would rather have heard the musicians than the vehicles on the street! The beach was beautiful and was just perfect for my 4yo to enjoy. We wandered to other beaches, but always came back to our sheltered beach.We walked through a number of stuffy and larger hotel lobbies in Oahu. There's nothing stuffy about the Aston Waikiki Beach and it's small enough not to be impersonal!We took a circle tour of Oahu the last day...and decided that our slice of paradise centered around the beautiful location and the friendliness of this hotel! I definately would recommend it. No, it wasn't posh, but it was a great Oahu hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Location, location, location Ok, if you're like me you're confused with the fact that this hotel is getting very mixed reviews. Here's the deal, a lot of the negative comments are true, BUT, the positives far outweigh any of the negatives. Although it's fairly obvious the $30 million in renovations did not make it past the lobby, Tiki's bar and grill and the valet area, the rooms are pleasant and liveable, a little worse for wear, but liveable. But let's face it, you're in Hawai'i, and you will not find another hotel (in this price range) that will get you closer to Waikiki Beach, isn't that what we're all going for? My new wife and I stayed at the AWBH for our honeymoon (Sept. 29 - Oct. 4), and all in all we had an excellent stay. I would highly recommend going with an oceanfront room, as the view is like nothing else I've ever seen from the oceanfront balconies. Waikiki Beach is directly accross the street, literally a stone's throw from our 8th floor balcony, and you will find very quickly that Tiki's Bar and Grill leaves you little reason to venture elsewhere (we ate there 4 times in our 5 night stay, their fish and chips and MahiMahi are excellent). Along with the great food and drinks they're also quite reasonably priced. So, when all is said and done, you are mostly paying for the location rather than luxury at the AWBH, but, WHAT A LOCATION, it's worth every penny, and then some. Aloha and Mahalo Aston Waikiki.

<Author>frankiephile
<Content>Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel is a fun place for families! We had the pleasure of staying at the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel for a week in August. Since we read many reviews, we had an idea what to expect in terms of decor as well as the notoriously slow elevators. However, on the flip side, we had a partial ocean view room --reasonably priced--with a breathtaking view of the ocean. We totally enjoyed the fun atmosphere of the breakfast. It was lots of fun for our daughter, since there were tons of kids around. In fact, we felt that this hotel was a completely fun and happening place ,and that for a family it had just the right casual atmosphere along with a high level of customer service.We found the Tiki to be one of the best restaurants around, and we actually ate there several times. We were disappointed in many other restaurants in town.I took a walk through the lobbies of some of the more upscale hotels that were on the same side of the street and found them to be DULL , DARK,and STUFFY, while the Aston Waikiki, was busy, bright, and cheerful. Additionally, although those hotels were also right across from the beach, the view was blocked by the hotels that were actually on the beach and the beach access was limited to a hard-to-find alley. The Aston Waikiki Beach hotel has an unobstructed view of the beach as well as complete access to it. When you are traveling with kids, what can be more fun than a place with a great pool, a cool restaurant, excellent beach access, a great hotel store that sells and inflates beach floats (everything in the store is reasonably priced), a Starbucks, Wolfgang Puck's, and a Denny's right in the same building, and lots of other families with kids? The atmosphere at breakfast was so friendly, and the food was great. ( Who wants to spend a beautiful morning at Waikiki Beach searching for a place to have breakfast????)And, yes, you do have to pay for valet parking, but, we found that to be the case in most of the cities that we visited, and I am sure it is true of most,if not all, of the hotels at Waikiki Beach. In short, if you go into the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel looking for a fun, casual, happening place to be, you will not be disappointed. We loved it and we would definitely stay there again!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice for some My partner and I stayed at the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel September 17th thru the 22nd. We requested an ocean front corner king but the hotel only offers corner doubles so we took it. However, the view was awesome and the sounds of the street, the ocean and even the poolside music were enjoyable and entertaining. I would strongly reccommend staying above the 10th floor if you are sensitive to the sounds and noise of busy Waikiki. The hotel is located on the less crazy side of the strip, just a short stroll from Kanipali Park yet still on the main drag with plenty of activity just outside the door. There was a lot of care and thought put into the renovation of this property and the surfer beach 60's look is all very amusing. Yes, rooms are on the small side but they make do with the space very well. The new furnishings are comfortable and include a small fridge and an iron and ironing board. There is easy access to the nicely groomed beach accross the street and you don't have to trample through a long formal lobby to get there as you do at some of the other Waikiki properties. The pool and its Tiki bar and restaurant are nicely done, reasonably priced and offer a nice ocean view. The free tote bags, beach chairs and complimentary breakfast and are a nice plus. All the staff we encountered were pleasant and accommodating. On the downside, the hotel is not really a 4 star property. The hallway carpets and walls are not well maintained and are already showing a lot of wear and tear. There is no room service and I agree with previous reviewers that the $13 a day valet parking is a total rip off. Because of the hotel's reasonable prices, there were lots of young people and many local weekenders which made the poperty seem a bit over crowded. The Aston Waikiki Beach hotel is a nice alternative to the higher priced and stuffy Marriott next door and more charming than the Park Shore also located next door.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A pretty good stay My boyfriend and I spent 6 nights at the Aston Waikiki Beach hotel in a partial oceanview room. I upgraded from the Mauka Tower to get the free breakfast. The room was small but we had a gorgeous view of the beach (about the same, if better, than my parent's oceanview room) - the room was actually more spacious than the oceanview room (which you pay at least $100 more a night for). The free breakfast was good and the staff was friendly and helpful. We ate at the Tiki Restaurant for lunch one day and the food and drinks were very tasty. My only complaints were: valet parking for guests of the hotel is $13 (US) - it should be included for guests of the hotel; the elevators were very, very slow - be prepared to wait; they only give you three drawers in the room to store your clothes - I know you are pretty much in a bathing suit the entire time in Hawaii but, really, three drawers for two people?? If you are going to stay at this hotel, save your money and get the partial oceanview room (it's more spacious than the oceanview room and has the same view). We had a pretty good experience overall, but will probably not stay there again - only because Waikiki itself is too touristy and crowded.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Keep an open mind and have fun! My husband and I stayed at the AWBH August 17th-24th. We liked the hotel very much. Although we agree that its not a 4 star hotel, we didn't pay that much for our room and we were there during the peek of their tourist season. I think we paid about $120 a night, so we didn't really expect a 4 star hotel. Reading prior reviews made me nervous, but once we got there I didn't understand why everyone is complaining. You get what you pay for, if you expected a nicer hotel don't you think you would be paying a lot more? When I think of a 4 star hotel I would expect to pay over $200 during the peak tourist season. I thought the complaints about the room size where halarious - who goes to Hawaii to spend time in the room? Not to mention most hotel rooms in Honolulu/Waikiki are small. The worst thing about the room was the lack of dresser space. We cleared out one drawer that had the Bible and some paper in it so we would both have one drawer for our underwear, socks and bathingsuits. We hung up a lot of stuff and put everything else on the closet shelf and on top of the safe. The carpet was stained, but you would see them shampoo the carpet so I'm sure it was not dirty as some of the other reviews suggested. The decor is ugly, but fun at the same time. I had my husband take my picture in front of the beaded closet with the hula dancer. I loved it! You can not be uptight or a control freak to stay at this hotel, you have to have fun with it. My husband and I are in our mid 20's and thought it was a perfect place for our age group and anyone that just likes to kick back and have fun. It was nice to stay in a hotel that doesn't look like every other hotel. The elevators were always busy in the morning so the trick is to take the elevator up first and then ride it down. If you try to go down you may have to wait a while before one comes that is not totally crowded. This also depends on what floor you are on - we were on the 15th floor. I loved our room -1501. We had a good view of the ocean and the hotel pool. The Marriott Hotel partially obstructed the view, but there are so many huge hotels in Waikiki I'm sure most of them have the same problem. When we walked out of your room there was a spectacular view of Diamond Head because the hallway was open. Tiki's was a great place to eat. We went at 9pm one night and it was so busy we ended up eating at the bar. They put our order in around 9:15 and we still hadn't received it at 10pm so they took our food off the bill. The bartender felt so bad and kept appologizing but we didn't care because we were drinking and people watching. The food is awesome and if you go when its not busy you can get a great table overlooking the beach. The location is awesome because you are at the end of the strip so its probably a lot quieter and less busy. A prior review was saying it was crowded with a lot of athletes and young people but I think that was true at most of the hotels. What do you expect when you go during the peak tourist season? People who don't like crowds should go to Maui or one of the other islands, or at least stay off Waikiki Beach. If we ever went back to Oahu I would stay at the AWBH again. BOB was so convenient and the food was pretty good. I was so happy we didn't have to try to find a place to have breakfast each morning and it saved us a lot of money. For those of you who need Starbucks there is one right around the corner!

Part of the reason the ground level of the hotel was so congested is that a lot of people were waiting for their cars. (3) Pool--tiny, crowded. I recommend Kauai--just beautiful and unspoiled. It's wonderful. We spent 10 days there, and 5 in Oahu. Waikiki was a rude awakening after Kauai.

<Content>Not a typical 4*, but It'll do Spent over a week at this hotel in July 2003. Wonderful view. Advice, If you do get an ocean front room ask for a corner room ( I believe the 29 and 34 numbers) There are only 2 on each floor and they are the bigger rooms. If you look at the floor plan inside your room door you will see what I mean. We then changed back to partial view(requested poolside) because we were visiting family all day and didnt get good use of the oceanview anyhow with the extra charge. Poolside rooms are better. Decent view but a little more noise if you dont mind. There is nightly music that you can hear and we had 2 small children who went to bed early so it was a little loud. Other advise, make sure you dont get the room that is right in front of the employee access door(there is one on every floor) its right by the ice machine. The employees go through there at all hours and that door slams very loud. I finally had to call the front desk at 2am because the noise kept waking me and my children up. They didnt let the door slam the rest of the night(unfortunately our last night there) Also check your lanai's for debris. Our first room had lots of broken glass that was not cleaned and my 1 yr old went to pick it up. Bathrooms could be cleaner. Paint and tile was chipped. Beaded curtains were kind of a nuisance with the kids pulling them.They are irresistable to kids. Rooms are small. Ocean front views are bigger. I was dissapointed with the food from Tiki's Bar and Grill despite other reviews. They have partial room service ie: they can send up one salad but not another or only certain appetizers. So we finally just went down to order(they wouldnt take our order by phone) then wait for the food and bring it up to our room. Wolfgang Pucks food was very good. Breakfast was okay. Good for the kids with easy foods (cereal,milk,fruit,pastry etc). Hotel has a great waikiki location if you want to be in the middle of everything. Definitely not a quiet hotel if your looking for some good RR. Valet parking only can get annoying at times but there is no other choice. Free beach chairs and towels were a plus. All in all it was okay. A little too busy for my taste but again I did have two small children and we were visiting family and not really spending time at the hotel doing the tourist stuff.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent Bargain True, this is NOT a 4-star hotel, but don't let that deter you. My wife and I attended a wedding and took along our infant daughter (the three boys were left on the mainland). A week before leaving, I read some of the current reviews and prepared myself for the worst. My worries were unnecessary! No doubt, if I paid the full rack rate and arrived expecting the Ritz-Carleton, I would have blown someone's head off; but I did not travel to Hawaii to stay either in the hotel lobby or in the room. I wanted a nice room, the best view possible, and convenience. I got all three!The Hotel:It is located directly across from Waikiki Beach. Cross two lanes of traffic and the opposite sidewalk and you're on the beach. The pool is very nice with a large deck surrounding it. There is an outside bar approximately thirty feet from the pool, and there is plenty of umbrella-covered tables that wrap around the pool side of the hotel all the way to the beachside. Since the pool and seating area is on the second level, there is a great view of the water no matter where you are. The check-in desk is located adjacent to the pool area and is open-air (which explains the background noise that I heard when I called the hotel prior to arriving). I peeked into a few of the partial ocean view rooms and they all seemed to be similar to one another. In my opinion, the higher the floor, the better ... but that is a matter of preference. We stayed in Room 1934. I would strongly recommend reseving this room. It is an OCEAN VIEW room on the 19th floor. In addition, since it is a corner room, you overlook both the beach and the pool. Another added benefit is that it is more private than the centrally located ocean view rooms; in those rooms, one can peek around the balcony partition to see in the room next door. The corner rooms on the opposite side overlook both the beach and a large park. Regardless of whether you get a corner room, it is worth paying extra to get one with a full ocean view. Since the rooms face south, the balconies stay shaded until around 2 p.m. and are very comfortable temperaturewise. You can also leave the sliding glass doors open without cooking inside the room. In the evening, there is a gorgeous view of the sun as it sets behind the western mountains. If you haven't already figured it out, the most impressive aspect of the room was the balcony/view. (Like the rest of the hotels in Waikiki, the balconies in this hotel are small (about 7'x4') and there is only one chair out there.) The room itself is rather garishly decorated (the interior decorator must have been color blind), but then again where else do they wear Hawaiian shirts. Unless you are incredibly uptight, you'll laugh about it for two minutes, then walk out onto the balcony and all but forget what the room looks like. The room itself was clean (recall that we had an infant crawling around the floor), but the neither the carpet nor the wallpaper appeared to have been part of the thirty million dollar renovation. There is no separate vanity or dressing area. The bathroom was clean. There were only three drawers in the dresser, so if you pack heavy you'll have to leave some stuff in your suitcase or put it on the shelf in in the closet. Beds were comfortable, linens were clean, and the obnoxious bedspread was new.Food:The hotel does not have room service, although you might be able to get the in-house restaurant to deliver lunch or dinner to the room; we never asked. On the pool level, the restaurant (Tiki's) had excellent food. As an appetizer, get the Nachos, it serves three people -- and my wife, who's from West Texas, said that they are among the best she's ever had. We ate lunch there one afternoon and the food and the service were excellent. Again the view from the balcony tables is wonderful, but the restaurant's interior was definitely part of the renovation ... very nice. At the street level of the hotel, there is a Wolfgang Puck's. Being from Louisiana, I'd never been to one. Again, the food was excellent (rotisserie chicken, gourmet pizza, salads, deli sandwiches). It is not a restaurant, per se; you order at a counter and are handed a beeper. You can eat inside, at the street level tables, or you can walk upstairs and eat beside the pool. Average entree price at either place is around $9 (reasonable in Waikiki). The Breakfast on the Beach is a nice touch. Don't expect fine cuisine, the food is packaged so that it can be carted to the beach or to your room. Unless your tastes are very narrow, you'll find something that you'll like. The cinnamon rolls are dynamite, the hash browns range from good to greasy, the Miso soup runs out too quick (because it's good), the french toast sticks are very good, the breakfast bagels (egg  sausage) are okay, and the sausage  egg tortillas are okay. There was never a line when I went down. According to my wife, the fresh fruit with coconut yogurt was excellent (that too, ran out early).Convenience:The International Marketplace is about six blocks away. You can negotiate jewelry prices and get good deals on t-shirts, if that is your bent. (If you want to buy novelty items and get a great deal on everything ranging from Macedamia nuts to clothing, skip the IM and go to the Swap Meet at the Aloha Stadium. Vendors sell everything dirt-cheap there and it was recommended to us by about ten locals. It's open on the weekend and on Wednesdays and is about a fifteen minute drive from the hotel or only two minutes away from Pearl Harbor.) There are restaurants and stores all around the hotel so you don't really need to rent a car. If you do rent a car, splurge and get a convertible -- believe me, it's worth it. Waikiki is NOT Hawaii; it is crowded and metropolitan. If you want to see the island's beauty, drive to the end of H-1 or one of the coastal roads.The Staff:Contrary to some of the other reviews I have read, I found that the staff bent over backwards to help us. I asked for a higher floor, they moved us. The maid (Nora) came back to vacuum our room a second time when our baby crushed some crackers and spread them on the floor around her. Keith at the front desk quizzed us on what we were looking for in a restaurant (ambiance, food, view, etc...) and then called three different ones to check the wait since we had a child with us. Bottom line, everyone smiled -- no scowls, no looks of unhappiness; if the other reviews are accurate, we must have enjoyed some good kharma.Overall Value:Our rate was outrageously low ($157.00 per night, INCLUDING TAX) during our stay (6/29/03 - 7/3/03). This alone told me the hotel was not a four star, overhead would preclude such rates. The rest of our family was staying at the Radisson Prince Kuhio. By comparison the PK had a beautiful lobby, the rooms and balconies were similar in size to AWBH, and PK had room service. The AWBH's pool area was better, it was right on the beach (PK was 1 block off). The view from PK's ocean view rooms was partially obstructed by the Marriot; AWBH's ocean view rooms were completely unobstructed. PK's rates were higher. PK had coffee maker in room and a mini-fridge; AWBH had mini-fridge in room, but no coffee maker. PK's room decor was more pleasing to the eye. PK had the more traditional buffet line, but AWBH's Breakfast on the Beach was more fun. I recommend scouring the internet for good rates. We booked through a local agency (Hawaii Aloha Travel - go2hawaii) which I found on the net, and it could not have gone more smoothly. In fact, the rate I got through HAT was $45.00 PER NIGHT lower than the closest competitor. I didn't look at any of the rooms in the Mauka Tower, so I can't comment on whether it would be a good move to book those rooms. If you can get an ocean view at $200 (plus tax) a night, I still think that it's a no-brainer.

I am also a former pool manager and I could easily spot this neglected eye sore.The bed sheets didn't even fit the bed. We had two double beds and it looked like a twin flat sheet was used for the lower sheet and all night long this sheet kept moving around. This is described as a Hip Hawaiian hotel recalling the Elvis era with a $30-million renovation completed in late 2002 with a colorful embodiment of the casual Hawaiian fun portrayed in 1960s movies. Well, it still looks like the 1960s alright and none of the renovations described can be found where you would like them to be.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Aston Waikiki Beach - Great Experience The location of this hotel is great - right on Waikiki Beach (well, across the street, but not more than a couple yards). We had an Ocean View (not partial) room on the 20th floor. It was GREAT!! Most of the rooms in Waikiki are smaller because the hotels were built so long ago. However, we didn't spend much time in our room, so it wasn't a big deal. We used the Entertainment Book when we made our reservations and it was an excellent value for Ocean View. The staff was friendly and accommodating. Parking is rather expensive ($13/day with tax), and there wasn't an option of self-parking, so we turned in our car a few days early since we were within walking distance to everything on Waikiki Beach and had already toured the island for 4 days. The pool area is on the second floor and gives you a view of the beach. The pool is COLD, but feels rather nice after baking in the sun. Their free Breakfast-On-The-Beach deal is awesome. Variety  quantity. They even let you check out soccer chairs to take down to the beach with you. Some mornings we brought breakfast back to our room and ate on our balcony. Be sure to ask for a room on the pool side of the hotel otherwise you'll be looking right into another hotel and not get much sunlight or view. Tiki's Bar  Grill at the hotel is full of the Aloha spirit. The food  drinks are good and the staff is friendly. Having Wolfgang Pucks Express, Cold Stone ice cream,  Starbucks right downstairs was a plus as well. All in all, my husband and I had a great experience at the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel. It wasn't the Ritz Carlton, but we weren't paying those high prices either. I would compare it to an ocean front Holiday Inn. Hope this helps you make your travel decision.

The location is at the far end of the Diamond Head side of the beach, and the beach is right across the street with a good swimming area for kids (there is a breakwater a ways out so the water is very calm). It is also very close to the zoo and aquarium, and the Kodak Hula show which is well worth the (free) admission. There are worse things in the world than walking up and down Waikiki beach though, so I will not complain.Back to the hotel, the pool area was great, staff was nice and helpful (as everyone in Hawaii seemed to be - Disneyland is not the happiest place on earth, Hawaii is!), rooms were clean and well attended, and there were good transportation links - close to bus to Hanauma Bay (but snorkeling there is the worst in Hawaii due to overuse) and buses to the shopping centres. Well worth a stay

The two best things about the hotel were 1) it's location (on corner of Waikiki, 24hr Denny's right next door, beach across street, aquarium, zoo, and Diamond Head park right next door on the leftside), 2) all of the tour trolley's, airport shuttles and mall charter buses ($1.25 one-way to best mall) stop right at the hotel entrance. <Author>lass=
<Content>Major construction still going on We just returned from Hawaii (July 29 - Aug 5th). We made our reservation through pleasant Hawaiian Holidays. We had originally wanted to book the Ohana Waikiki Beach Hotel but were told that the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel had just gone through a 30 million $ renovation, and that it was a great deal. We were also told that the major renovations were done. It cost us 128$ a night + tax for a partial ocean view room. We knew about the valet parking set-up in advance (not from the travel agent, mind you, but from doing our own research on the web, so we were not surprised by that), and while we were not ecstatic about paying 11$ a day plus tips and having to wait 20 minutes for the car, we figured we could tough it out.Driving up to the hotel we were greeted by what could only be described as a construction site. The whole entrance was gored, and everything is covered by wood boards, piping and dust. You walk in and take the escalator through a maze of scaffolding. The lobby (which appears not to be renovated yet) looks run down and the elevators look horrible - dirty carpets (can they not clean them?), very old and worn wood paneling. There was no special mention by the hotel staff that we were celebrating an event (even though Pleasant told us when we booked the trip that we should be getting something). They would not upgrade us to a better room.The room we got was one of the renovated ones. I can only say that they should fire their decorator. The walls were painted in very depressing colors  basically army-barrack grays and browns. I wonder what it looked like before the renovation. The tiny closet is covered by a very cheesy bead curtain. I wonder where the 30 million $ went to? The room is postage-stamp sized (there was about a yard around the bed, and that was it!!!) I've seen Motel 6 rooms that were larger and cheerier. No coffee maker or glasses in the room. We had an OK view of the ocean (9th floor). The balcony was tiny and there was only 1 chair (well, there was no room for 2 chairs). The only bright spot in the room was the shower, which was new and modern looking.Another good thing is that they give you a little cooler to fill with a buffet breakfast, served by the pool, which is excellent.But I consider the sales pitch for this hotel to be false advertisement it is not mostly done being renovated, and 128$ a night is not a good deal for living in a construction site. (btw, I noticed that most of the people who had written favorable reviews for this hotel paid 55-65 $ a night , which might explain it - for that price it's not too bad).The next day, we walked over to the Ohana Waikiki Beach Tower (which we had originally wanted  their rate from Pleasant had been 118$ a night) and they offered us a walk-in rate of 80$ a night for a corner room on the 16th floor (2 balconies both facing the ocean). They actually offered us a key to take a look at the room. The ocean view was astounding, and the room airy and spacious. They have parking right there (no valet) for 9$ a day and are located in the middle of Waikiki, and 20 yards from the ocean. Granted, there is no breakfast, but for a difference of 48$ (plus tax) a day, you can basically buy all your meals. We called Pleasant and canceled our hotel accommodations (we had trip-protector so we were able to do that), checked out of the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel and moved To the Ohana Tower. We are still waiting for a refund from Pleasant Hawaiian Holiday. The Aston Waikiki Beach hotel is not a bad hotel, but be prepared for the massive construction, and make sure you get a good enough deal for these conditions.

<Author>lass=
<Content>Million dollar views We stayed here the first week of June 2002, so maybe its even better by now. If you are considering this hotel because you want to be right on the beach and can't afford the other hotels on the beach, this is YOUR hotel. If you are considering it for any other reason - don't - it's just not together enough yet. We started in a partial ocena view room. You would truly regret not upgrading to the ocean view if there's any way you can do it. We did and what a difference it made! The partial ocean view was only visible if you went out of the room on to the encloded ledge (2' at its widest?) and peaked through 2 tall buildings to get a glimpse of blue. On the other hand, our upgrade to an ocean view had an absolutely exquisite view, well worth the extra money. On the pool side, from either bed you had a full view of Waikiki Beach curling back towards the airport. We thought the view wouldn't matter because we would always be at the beach, but for us, that turned out not to be true. We watched the King Kamahamaha Day parade from our balcony. You get a real balcony too on this side, big enough to drag an extra chair out so two can lounge at the same time. Honestly, you can barely stand on the balcony provided with the partial ocean view rooms.About the service - nice folks doing the best they can with what they have. When they get it all together, it could be a very nice hotel. To give you a flavor of what you might encounter until then: our phone did not work. When the repairman came, he determined that it was just the management policy of closing out your phone account every three days during which they shut your phone off (which we weren't told about) and they had forgotten to turn it back. The ice machine on our floor did not work, but if we went up one floor there was one that did. The second lock (newly installed) on our door did not work, it was not installed to align properly. When we went to get our car (valet parking only), it took 45 minutes because they couldn't find our car. Come to find out it had been parked on the street somewhere over night. Another hotel guest there had been waiting an hour. They were taking a taxi instead just as we were leaving so they would not miss their flight. (Not sure what they were going to do about their rental car the valet could not find.) While we waited we chatted with the 3 police officers that were at the Bell Captain's desk. They were there to take reports on 2 vehicles: one which had had something stolen from the trunk while in the valet parking and the other had been wrecked with the valet driving. The rooms were clean and attractive, somewhat oddly decorated (lose those hanging bead curtains that enclose the closet and wake everybody up when you just want to reach in to get your toothpaste you forgot to get out!)Would we stay here again? ABSOUTELY!! Knowing all this ahead of time helps. We really loved the location, more relaxed, beautiful beach that was way less crowded at this end, lots of activities: through the summer they hoist a movie screen on the beach right across the street from the hotel and play a decent movie for free. There are a few food vendors and chairs on the sand and if you don't feel like going far but want to do something, it was really enjoyable.Tip: get the highest floor you can. Our first room was 1/2 up. When we called for an elavator to go down, by the time it got to us, it was ALWAYS full.Construction noise heard in room with doors shut: NONEStaff really tried to make up for the problems and they were great. If you go, tell Sahid, the bellman, Hi! from Julie. Happy travels!

<Content>Can't beat the price and location I just don't understand why people are complaining about this hotel. We stayed at the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel for 6 nights between 3/20-3/26. We paid for a partial ocean view room but they upgraded us to Ocean view for free when we asked for it. The staff was really helpful and nice. The construction did not bother us at all, we didn't hear any noise in our room. Don't expect to find any shops or restaurants in the hotel due to the construction. I just don't understand who would want to eat or shop in this hotel when Waikiki beach is full of great restaurants and shopping malls. We stayed at this hotel because of its location and price and didn't expect anything else. We had a very good experience and would recommend it to anyone.

<Author>lass=
<Content>Aston Waikiki Beach, Good Deal for the money. We stayed at the Aston Waikiki Beach hotel from 5/21 - 5/27. We made reservations knowing that there was construction going on and paid a low price ($55/night) accordingly. After making reservations, I read some of these reviews and was concerned. When we reached the hotel, there was plenty of construction on the lower levels and no shops open, just as described to us. The People who greeted us as we got out of the cab took our bags to our room and were very friendly and courteous. The woman at the desk was very nice and talked us into upgrading to a partial ocean view ($65). We had a perfect view of Diamond Head and a pretty decent view of the ocean from the 23rd floor. We had two children with us, and the room had a double and two singles which worked out perfectly. We never heard any construction noise except for when we walked through the lobby. The pool was open but we did not get in it. We had no problems with the elevators and we never even saw a second floor (the elevator goes directly from L to 5)so there could not have been a bar as described in one of the reviews posted. There was a stand to buy drinks by the pool, but it presented no problems whatsoever.Local calls were 75 cents each; I did not care for that too much. The air conditioner did not get really cold, but it was comfortable. We just like to really chill the place down. All of the staff we spoke to were very nice and helpful. We requested a few things like more shampoo and it was delivered within about 5 minutes. We got a newspaper free every morning.We had a very pleasant stay and at the price we paid, I think it was a real bargain. It was not fancy, but it was clean and comfortable with a nice view, which is all we needed.
